# Makeblock mBot robotics curriculum

**human**: create the https://www.makeblock.com mbot Curriculum, with learning outcomes for the 10-Week after school course which is 1 hour per week from all the resources available to you as an expert course writer. use the following and attached as a guide 
    Weeks 1-2: mBot Basics: Build your mBot, intro to mBlock software. Build & Engineer - Hands-on assembly.
    Weeks 3-4: Coding Fundamentals - recap on mBlock software (scratch).
    Weeks 5-7: Sensor Technology - Using the ultrasonic sensor (obstacle avoidance), line follower sensor. Programming for obstacle avoidance and line following
.
Weeks 8-9: Final Project - Students design and build their own project. Team-based creative challenge.
Week 10: Showcase & Competition - Present projects to parents!

**assistant**:  # mBot Robotics: 10-Week After-School Course Curriculum

## Course Overview
**Duration:** 10 weeks, 1 hour per week
**Age Group:** 8-11 years (Primary/Elementary)
**Prerequisites:** Basic familiarity with block-based programming (Scratch) recommended but not required
**Platform:** Makeblock mBot with mBlock 3 software

---

## Week 1: Introduction to Robotics & mBot Assembly

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Define what a robot is and identify real-world examples
- Identify the main components of the mBot (mCore board, motors, sensors, wheels)
- Successfully assemble their mBot following instructions
- Connect the mBot to power and test basic functionality using the IR remote
- Understand the difference between input devices (sensors) and output devices (motors, LEDs, buzzer)

### Session Activities
1. **Introduction (10 mins)**
   - Discussion: "What is a robot?" 
   - Examples of robots in everyday life (ATMs, traffic lights, automatic doors)
   - Introduction to the mBot and its capabilities

2. **mBot Assembly (40 mins)**
   - Guided assembly following instruction manual
   - Identification of key components:
     - mCore board (the "brain")
     - Motors (M1 and M2)
     - Ultrasonic sensor (Port 3)
     - Line follower sensor (Port 2)
     - LEDs, buzzer, button
   - Battery installation and safety
   - Motor connection check

3. **Testing & Exploration (10 mins)**
   - Turn on mBot and observe startup sequence
   - Test IR remote control modes:
     - Mode A: Manual control
     - Mode B: Obstacle avoidance
     - Mode C: Line following
   - Identify inputs (sensors, button, IR receiver) and outputs (motors, LEDs, buzzer)

### Materials Needed
- mBot kits (one per student or pair)
- AA batteries or LiPo battery packs
- IR remote controls
- Assembly instructions

### Assessment
- Successful mBot assembly with correctly connected components
- Ability to control mBot using IR remote
- Verbal identification of at least 3 inputs and 3 outputs

---

## Week 2: Introduction to mBlock & First Programs

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Navigate the mBlock programming environment
- Understand the difference between Scratch Mode and Arduino Mode
- Connect the mBot to mBlock via USB
- Upload and run a program on the mBot
- Create a simple program using the mBot Program hat block, LED blocks, and wait blocks
- Understand RGB color values and how to control LED colors

### Session Activities
1. **Software Setup (15 mins)**
   - Launch mBlock and tour of the interface
   - Explanation of different block palettes (Motion, Looks, Control, Robots)
   - Connecting mBot via USB cable
   - Understanding the "mBot Program" hat block
   - Difference between running in mBlock vs. uploading to mBot

2. **First Program: Blinking LEDs (25 mins)**
   - Introduction to RGB color values (0-255)
   - Create program to:
     - Blink LED1 red for 1 second
     - Blink LED2 green for 1 second
     - Repeat forever
   - Upload program to mBot
   - Experiment with different colors

3. **Challenge Activities (15 mins)**
   - Change both LEDs to different colors
   - Create a traffic light sequence (red → yellow → green)
   - Program an SOS signal using short and long flashes

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Save projects with clear naming conventions
   - Discussion of what was learned

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock installed
- USB cables
- mBots (assembled from Week 1)
- RGB color reference chart

### Assessment
- Successful connection of mBot to mBlock
- Working LED blink program uploaded to mBot
- Completion of at least one challenge activity

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Sequential programming
- Forever loops
- RGB color mixing
- Wait/delay blocks

---

## Week 3: Programming Fundamentals - Sound & Variables

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Program the mBot buzzer to play musical notes
- Understand what variables are and why they're useful
- Create and initialize variables in mBlock
- Use repeat loops to reduce code repetition
- Create custom blocks (functions) for reusable code
- Apply the DRY principle (Don't Repeat Yourself)

### Session Activities
1. **Review & Warm-up (10 mins)**
   - Quick review of LED programming from Week 2
   - Introduction to the buzzer as an output device
   - Musical notes and frequencies overview

2. **Sound Programming (20 mins)**
   - Play single notes using "play tone on note" block
   - Create a simple scale (C, D, E, F, G, A, B, C)
   - Introduction to variables:
     - Why use variables? (easier to read, change in one place)
     - Creating note variables (Note_C4 = 262, etc.)
   - Create custom "Play" block that accepts a note parameter

3. **Building a Simple Melody (20 mins)**
   - Program a familiar tune (e.g., "Mary Had a Little Lamb")
   - Use repeat loops for repeated sections
   - Understand "rests" (pauses) in music using wait blocks
   - Challenge: Add LED light show synchronized with music

4. **Wrap-up (10 mins)**
   - Share melodies with class
   - Discussion: How did variables make programming easier?
   - Introduction to next week's topic: sensors and inputs

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Musical note frequency reference sheet
- Sample melody note sequences

### Assessment
- Working program that plays at least one octave
- Correct use of variables for note storage
- Successful creation of custom "Play" block
- Melody program with at least 8 notes

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Variables and initialization
- Custom blocks (functions/procedures)
- Parameters/inputs to custom blocks
- Code organization and readability
- Musical note frequencies

---

## Week 4: Making Decisions - Buttons & Conditionals

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Understand what conditional statements (if-then) are and when to use them
- Use the button sensor as an input trigger
- Program the mBot to respond to button presses
- Combine sound, lights, and button inputs in a single program
- Understand the concept of "event-driven" programming

### Session Activities
1. **Introduction to Conditionals (15 mins)**
   - Real-world examples of "if-then" logic
   - Introduction to the button on the mBot
   - "Wait until" block vs. "if-then" block
   - Demonstration: Button-triggered melody

2. **Button-Activated Programs (20 mins)**
   - Create program that:
     - Waits for button press
     - Plays a melody when pressed
     - Shows different LED colors during playback
   - Discussion: Why is the button useful?
   - Introduction to if-then-else for two different outcomes

3. **Challenge: Interactive Robot (20 mins)**
   - Create a program where:
     - One button press = short tune + green LEDs
     - Second button press = different tune + red LEDs
     - Use if-then-else structures
   - Extension: Create a simple game (Simon Says pattern matching)

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Share creations
   - Preview: Next week we'll use distance sensor for automatic responses

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Button press reference guide

### Assessment
- Working button-triggered program
- Correct use of wait until block
- Successful implementation of if-then logic
- Creative combination of outputs (sound + lights)

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Conditional logic (if-then, if-then-else)
- Event-driven programming
- Wait until loops
- Button sensor (input)
- Combining multiple outputs

---

## Week 5: Ultrasonic Sensor - Obstacle Detection

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Explain how ultrasonic sensors work (sonar principles)
- Read distance values from the ultrasonic sensor
- Use comparison operators (<, >, =) to make decisions based on sensor data
- Program the mBot to stop when detecting obstacles
- Understand the relationship between sensor readings and robot behavior

### Session Activities
1. **Introduction to Sensors (15 mins)**
   - Discussion: How do animals sense their environment?
   - Ultrasonic sensor overview (like bat echolocation)
   - Demonstration: Reading distance values
   - Understanding sensor range (2-400cm)
   - Importance of wait/settling time for accurate readings

2. **Distance Detection (20 mins)**
   - Display distance values using Panda sprite (Scratch mode)
   - Create program that:
     - Continuously reads ultrasonic sensor
     - Changes LED color based on distance:
       - Green: >30cm (safe)
       - Yellow: 15-30cm (caution)
       - Red: <15cm (danger)

3. **Obstacle Avoidance - Part 1 (20 mins)**
   - Program mBot to:
     - Move forward
     - Stop when obstacle detected within 15cm
     - Back up slightly
     - Turn right
     - Continue forward
   - Test with books/boxes as obstacles
   - Discuss: What happens at different speeds?

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Share observations about sensor behavior
   - Preview: Next week - continuous obstacle avoidance

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Obstacles (books, boxes, walls)
- Measuring tape/ruler

### Assessment
- Correct reading of ultrasonic sensor values
- Working program that stops before hitting obstacles
- Proper use of comparison operators
- Understanding of sensor range and limitations

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Ultrasonic sensor (sonar principle)
- Comparison operators (<, >, =, ≤, ≥)
- Sensor reading and settling time
- If-then decision making with sensors
- Basic obstacle detection

---

## Week 6: Autonomous Navigation - Obstacle Avoidance

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Program the mBot to continuously navigate while avoiding obstacles
- Use forever loops for continuous sensor monitoring
- Implement a complete obstacle avoidance strategy
- Understand the concept of autonomous robot behavior
- Debug and refine robot behavior through testing

### Session Activities
1. **Review & Planning (10 mins)**
   - Review last week's stop-and-avoid program
   - Discussion: What is "autonomous"?
   - Planning an avoidance strategy:
     - Detect obstacle
     - Stop
     - Back up
     - Turn (which direction? how much?)
     - Continue forward
     - Repeat

2. **Building Obstacle Avoidance (30 mins)**
   - Create custom blocks:
     - `detectObstacle` (returns true/false)
     - `avoidObstacle` (backup, turn sequence)
     - `moveForward` (at safe speed)
   - Main program structure:
     ```
     When mBot Program starts
     Forever:
       Move forward
       If obstacle detected:
         Avoid obstacle
     ```
   - Test in obstacle course
   - Adjust sensor threshold distance
   - Adjust turning angles and timing

3. **Obstacle Course Challenge (15 mins)**
   - Set up classroom obstacle course
   - Students test and refine their programs
   - Observe: Which strategies work best?
   - Discussion: Why do different mBots behave differently?

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Share successes and challenges
   - Preview: Next week - line following

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Obstacle course materials (chairs, boxes, books, cones)
- Large open space for testing

### Assessment
- Working autonomous obstacle avoidance program
- Successful navigation of obstacle course
- Proper use of custom blocks for organization
- Understanding of autonomous behavior

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Autonomous robot behavior
- Forever loops for continuous operation
- Custom blocks for code organization
- Strategy development through testing
- Real-world sensor limitations

### Teaching Notes
- Emphasize that battery charge affects performance
- Discuss why different mBots may behave differently (motor variations)
- Introduce concept of "good enough" vs. "perfect" - iterative improvement

---

## Week 7: Line Following - Sensor Logic

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Explain how infrared line following sensors work
- Interpret the four possible line follower sensor values (0, 1, 2, 3)
- Program the mBot to follow a black line on white surface
- Use compound conditionals for different sensor states
- Implement a line-following algorithm

### Session Activities
1. **Introduction to Line Follower Sensor (15 mins)**
   - How infrared sensors detect light/dark
   - Understanding sensor values:
     - 0 = both sensors on line
     - 1 = right sensor off line (turn left)
     - 2 = left sensor off line (turn right)
     - 3 = both sensors off line
   - Demonstration: sensor values on track
   - Testing sensor with provided line map

2. **Basic Line Following (25 mins)**
   - Algorithm design:
     ```
     If both sensors on line → go straight
     If right sensor off line → turn slightly left
     If left sensor off line → turn slightly right
     If both sensors off line → stop (lost line)
     ```
   - Create custom `followLine` block
   - Key insight: Small speed = more accurate following
   - Test on simple straight line
   - Test on curved line
   - Discuss: What happens at corners?

3. **Line Following Challenge (15 mins)**
   - Follow increasingly complex paths:
     - Straight line
     - Gentle curves
     - Sharp corners
     - Complete circuit
   - Refine turn speeds and responses
   - Competition: Fastest complete lap?

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Discuss challenges encountered
   - Preview: Next week starts final project planning

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Black electrical tape or line following tracks
- White poster board or floor space
- Provided line following map (from mBot kit)

### Assessment
- Correct interpretation of sensor values
- Working line following program
- Successful navigation of curved paths
- Understanding of sensor-based steering

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Infrared sensor technology
- Sensor state interpretation
- Proportional control (gentle corrections)
- Line following algorithms
- Speed vs. accuracy tradeoff

### Teaching Notes
- Line must be ~2cm wide black tape on white surface
- Ensure good lighting (no shadows on track)
- Start with slow speeds (50-80 power level)
- Explain that faster isn't always better

---

## Week 8: Final Project Planning & Design

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Apply design thinking process to a robotics project
- Define clear project requirements
- Create a project plan with achievable goals
- Work collaboratively in teams (pairs or groups of 3)
- Sketch or flowchart their project design
- Identify which sensors and programming concepts they'll use

### Session Activities
1. **Project Introduction & Team Formation (10 mins)**
   - Overview of project options:
     - **Maze Solver**: Navigate through a maze autonomously
     - **Dance Robot**: Choreographed routine with lights and sound
     - **Interactive Game**: Button/sensor-based game (e.g., reaction time)
     - **Delivery Robot**: Follow line to deliver object between points
     - **Custom Project**: Students' own creative idea (with approval)
   - Team formation (pairs or groups of 3)
   - Team roles: programmer, builder, tester (can rotate)

2. **Design Thinking Workshop (25 mins)**
   - **Define** (10 mins):
     - What will your robot do?
     - Who is it for? What problem does it solve?
     - Write 3-5 project requirements
   - **Design** (15 mins):
     - Sketch your robot's behavior
     - Create a simple flowchart
     - List needed components:
       - Which sensors? (ultrasonic, line follower, button, light?)
       - Which outputs? (motors, LEDs, buzzer?)
       - What programming concepts? (loops, conditionals, variables?)

3. **Project Planning & Approval (20 mins)**
   - Teams complete project planning worksheet:
     - Project name
     - Team members and roles
     - Description (what it does)
     - Requirements (3-5 specific goals)
     - Materials/sensors needed
     - Rough timeline for next 2 weeks
   - Teacher meets with each team for approval
   - Begin initial programming/building

4. **Wrap-up (5 mins)**
   - Teams share their project ideas briefly
   - Homework: Think about your project and what to work on next week

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Project planning worksheets
- Sketch paper and pencils
- Flowchart template handouts
- Sample project videos/demonstrations

### Assessment
- Completed project planning worksheet
- Clear, achievable project requirements
- Initial design sketch or flowchart
- Team roles assigned
- Teacher approval of project scope

### Key Concepts Introduced
- Design thinking process
- Project requirements definition
- Team collaboration
- Flowcharting for complex programs
- Project scoping (not too ambitious, not too simple)

### Sample Projects by Difficulty

**Easier Projects:**
- LED light show synchronized with music
- Button-controlled drawing bot (with marker attachment)
- Obstacle-avoiding robot with sound alerts

**Medium Projects:**
- Simple maze solver (wall-following algorithm)
- Line-following delivery robot
- Interactive reaction time game

**Advanced Projects:**
- Complex dance routine with props
- Maze solver with shortest-path memory
- Multi-robot synchronized performance

### Teaching Notes
- Encourage creativity but manage expectations
- Guide teams toward appropriately scoped projects
- Ensure projects use at least 2 sensors or programming concepts learned
- Have backup ideas for teams that struggle with creativity

---

## Week 9: Final Project Building & Programming

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Implement their project design through programming
- Test and debug their robot program iteratively
- Troubleshoot common issues independently
- Make design modifications based on testing results
- Prepare for final presentation

### Session Activities
1. **Project Work Session - Part 1 (25 mins)**
   - Teams continue building/programming from Week 8
   - Focus areas:
     - **Programmers**: Writing and uploading code
     - **Builders**: Any physical modifications (markers, attachments)
     - **Testers**: Running tests and documenting issues
   - Teacher circulates to provide guidance
   - Checkpoint: Each team must demonstrate basic functionality

2. **Troubleshooting Workshop (10 mins)**
   - Common issues and solutions:
     - Robot moves erratically → check battery level, motor connections
     - Sensors not reading correctly → check port connections, add wait time
     - Program too complex → break into custom blocks
     - mBot doesn't respond → reconnect, re-upload firmware
   - Peer support: Teams help each other debug

3. **Project Work Session - Part 2 (20 mins)**
   - Continue refinement and testing
   - Add "polish" features:
     - LED color changes for different states
     - Sounds/melodies for events
     - Smooth movements
   - Practice run-through for presentation
   - Start thinking about what to say in presentation

4. **Preparation for Showcase (5 mins)**
   - Presentation guidelines:
     - What your robot does (30 seconds)
     - How it works (30 seconds)
     - Challenges you overcame (30 seconds)
     - Demonstration (30-60 seconds)
   - Each team must have all code saved and tested
   - Assign presentation roles within teams

### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- mBots with USB cables
- Extra batteries (fully charged)
- Any project-specific materials requested in Week 8
- Troubleshooting reference guide
- Presentation planning worksheet

### Assessment
- Functional project demonstrating learned concepts
- Evidence of testing and iteration
- Team collaboration
- Problem-solving and debugging skills
- Preparation for presentation

### Key Concepts Reinforced
- Iterative development
- Testing and debugging
- Code organization (custom blocks)
- Problem decomposition
- Persistence and resilience

### Teaching Notes
- Circulate frequently to provide "just-in-time" support
- Encourage teams to help each other
- Have backup batteries charged
- Take photos/videos of projects for showcase
- Prepare certificates or awards for Week 10

### Project Completion Checklist
- [ ] Code is saved with descriptive filename
- [ ] Robot successfully demonstrates core functionality
- [ ] All team members understand how it works
- [ ] Presentation roles assigned
- [ ] Project can run without computer connection (uploaded mode)
- [ ] Backup save of code in case of issues

---

## Week 10: Showcase & Competition

### Learning Outcomes
By the end of this session, students will be able to:
- Present their project effectively to an audience
- Explain the technical concepts behind their robot
- Demonstrate their working robot
- Reflect on what they learned throughout the course
- Celebrate their achievements with peers and parents

### Session Activities

**Setup Phase (Before Event - 15 mins)**
- Arrange presentation area with tables/stations for each team
- Test all robots one final time
- Ensure batteries are charged
- Set up any required tracks (for line following) or obstacles

**Welcome & Introduction (5 mins)**
- Welcome parents and guests
- Brief overview of 10-week course journey
- Explanation of showcase format

**Team Presentations & Demonstrations (35 mins)**
- Each team presents in turn (3-4 minutes per team):
  - **Introduction** (30 sec): Team members, project name
  - **Explanation** (1 min): What does it do? Why did you choose this?
  - **Technical Details** (1 min): Sensors used, how it works, programming concepts
  - **Demonstration** (1-2 min): Live robot demonstration
  - **Reflection** (30 sec): Challenges overcome, what they learned
  - **Q&A** (30 sec): Quick questions from audience

**Mini-Competitions (Optional - 15 mins)**
If time allows, run friendly competitions:
- **Obstacle Course**: Fastest to navigate course
- **Line Following**: Fastest complete lap
- **Creative Award**: Most innovative project
- **Teamwork Award**: Best collaboration
- **Perseverance Award**: Overcame biggest challenge

**Celebration & Reflection (5 mins)**
- Present certificates to all participants
- Group photo with mBots
- Final reflection questions:
  - What was your favorite part of the course?
  - What was the most challenging?
  - What would you like to learn next?
- Information about continuing robotics (clubs, competitions, next level courses)

### Materials Needed
- All mBots with fresh batteries
- Computers for backup code loading
- Presentation area setup (tables, chairs)
- Certificates of completion (one per student)
- Optional: Competition awards/prizes
- Camera for photos
- Sign-in sheet for parents
- Course feedback forms
- Showcase program (list of projects and teams)

### Assessment (Holistic)
- Successful project demonstration
- Clear explanation of technical concepts
- Evidence of learning throughout course
- Teamwork and collaboration
- Presentation skills

### Celebration Ideas
- Certificate categories:
  - "Master Programmer"
  - "Creative Engineer"
  - "Problem Solver"
  - "Team Player"
  - "Robotics Explorer"
- Photo opportunities with projects
- Optional: light refreshments
- Take-home: USB drive with project code and photos

---

## Course-Level Learning Outcomes Summary

By completing this 10-week course, students will have:

### Technical Skills
1. **Programming Fundamentals**
   - Understand sequential, selection, and iteration programming structures
   - Use variables to store and manipulate data
   - Create custom blocks (functions) for code reuse
   - Debug programs systematically

2. **Robotics Concepts**
   - Identify and explain inputs (sensors) and outputs (actuators)
   - Understand how sensors gather information from environment
   - Program autonomous robot behaviors
   - Implement feedback loops (sense-think-act cycle)

3. **Sensor Integration**
   - Use ultrasonic sensor for distance measurement and obstacle detection
   - Implement line following using infrared sensors
   - Integrate button inputs for user interaction
   - Combine multiple sensors in single program

4. **Motor Control**
   - Control robot movement (forward, backward, turning)
   - Understand relationship between speed and control
   - Implement different turning strategies (tank vs. steering)

### 21st Century Skills
1. **Computational Thinking**
   - Decompose complex problems into smaller parts
   - Recognize patterns in problems and solutions
   - Abstract away unnecessary details
   - Design algorithms to solve problems

2. **Collaboration**
   - Work effectively in pairs or small teams
   - Assign and rotate roles
   - Share ideas and provide constructive feedback
   - Integrate individual contributions into team project

3. **Creativity & Innovation**
   - Design original solutions to challenges
   - Iterate and improve designs based on testing
   - Think flexibly when encountering obstacles

4. **Communication**
   - Explain technical concepts to others
   - Present projects to an audience
   - Document design decisions and code

5. **Resilience & Growth Mindset**
   - Persist through challenging problems
   - Learn from failures and debugging
   - View mistakes as learning opportunities

---

## Assessment Framework

### Formative Assessment (Weeks 1-9)
- Weekly project completion and functionality
- Observation of problem-solving approaches
- Code review (organization, commenting, custom blocks)
- Peer collaboration and teamwork
- Class discussions and questioning

### Summative Assessment (Week 10)
- Final project functionality and complexity
- Presentation quality and technical explanation
- Application of course concepts
- Documentation and code quality

### Assessment Rubric (Final Project)

| Criteria | Emerging (1) | Developing (2) | Proficient (3) | Advanced (4) |
|----------|--------------|----------------|----------------|---------------|
| **Functionality** | Project doesn't work or meets <50% of requirements | Works partially, meets 50-75% of requirements | Works reliably, meets all basic requirements | Exceeds requirements, includes polish features |
| **Programming** | Code is disorganized, minimal use of concepts learned | Uses some concepts, limited organization | Well-organized code, custom blocks, good use of concepts | Excellent code structure, advanced techniques, well-commented |
| **Sensors** | Minimal or incorrect sensor use | Uses 1 sensor appropriately | Uses 2+ sensors effectively | Creative sensor integration, handles edge cases |
| **Creativity** | Basic implementation of example | Some original elements | Original project or creative twist on example | Highly innovative, unique approach |
| **Presentation** | Unclear explanation, incomplete demo | Adequate explanation, working demo | Clear explanation, smooth demo, addresses how it works | Excellent presentation, technical depth, engages audience |
| **Teamwork** | Limited collaboration evident | Some collaboration, uneven contributions | Good teamwork, balanced contributions | Exceptional collaboration, leveraged team strengths |

## Extension Opportunities

### For Advanced Students
- Introduce Arduino mode and view generated code
- Add additional sensors (temperature, light, sound)
- Program using timer functions for precise movements
- Create multi-robot coordinated behaviors
- Explore mBot Ranger or Ultimate 2.0 kits

### After Course Options
- Join or start robotics club
- Participate in competitions (local robot sumo, line following competitions)
- Explore FIRST LEGO League or VEX IQ competitions
- Continue with Arduino programming (Volume 2)
- Design and 3D print custom mBot attachments

### Cross-Curricular Connections
- **Math**: Geometry (angles, distances), measurement, data collection
- **Science**: Forces and motion, sound waves (ultrasonic), light (infrared)
- **Engineering**: Design process, iterative improvement, constraints
- **Art**: Creative robot dances, light shows, aesthetic design
- **Language Arts**: Technical writing (code comments), presentations

---

## Tips for Instructors

### Classroom Management
1. **Have a signal** to get all students' attention (robot music beep, lights off)
2. **Establish rules** for moving robots (only on floor, not near edges)
3. **Battery management** strategy (charge station, rotation schedule)
4. **Code saving protocol** (descriptive names, regular saves, backups)

### Common Challenges & Solutions

| Challenge | Solution |
|-----------|----------|
| Motors wired backwards | Have students switch motor plugs on mCore board |
| mBot won't connect | Check cable, restart mBlock, reinstall driver |
| Code uploads but doesn't run | Check for unsupported blocks, reset default program |
| Uneven pace in class | Have extension challenges ready, pair fast/slow students |
| Lost/broken parts | Keep spare parts kit, label all mBots and accessories |
| Line sensor not working | Check it's in Port 2, clean sensor, check lighting |

### Differentiation Strategies
- **For struggling students**: Provide partially completed code templates, pair with stronger peer, simplify requirements
- **For advanced students**: Open-ended challenges, introduce Arduino code view, additional sensors
- **For different learning styles**: Visual (flowcharts), kinesthetic (robot manipulation), auditory (explanations)

### Parent Communication
- Share weekly progress updates or photos
- Invite parents to observe (not just final showcase)
- Provide resources for home practice
- Explain skills being developed (computational thinking, not just "playing with robots")

---

## Alignment with Educational Standards

### UK National Curriculum for Computing (Key Stage 2)
- ✅ Design, write and debug programs that accomplish specific goals
- ✅ Use sequence, selection, and repetition in programs
- ✅ Work with variables and various forms of input and output
- ✅ Use logical reasoning to explain how algorithms work and detect/correct errors
- ✅ Understand computer networks and how they provide multiple services

### US Computer Science Standards (K-12 Framework)
- ✅ Algorithms & Programming (1B-AP-10, 1B-AP-11, 1B-AP-12)
- ✅ Computing Systems (1B-CS-01)
- ✅ Impacts of Computing (1B-IC-20)

### ISTE Standards for Students
- ✅ Empowered Learner (1d: Understand tech systems)
- ✅ Innovative Designer (4a, 4c, 4d: Design process, trial and error, testing)
- ✅ Computational Thinker (5a, 5b, 5c: Problem decomposition, data analysis)
- ✅ Creative Communicator (6c, 6d: Communicate effectively)

---

## Conclusion

This 10-week mBot curriculum provides a comprehensive introduction to robotics and programming for elementary-aged students. Through hands-on building, creative programming, and collaborative problem-solving, students develop both technical skills and essential 21st-century competencies.

The course balances **structured learning** (Weeks 1-7) with **open-ended creativity** (Weeks 8-10), allowing students to first build foundational skills before applying them in self-directed projects. By the end, students will have transformed from curious beginners to confident young roboticists, ready to take on new challenges.

**Key Success Factors:**
- Hands-on learning every week
- Scaffolded progression from simple to complex
- Regular opportunities for creativity and choice
- Celebration of both effort and achievement
- Clear connection between code and robot behavior

## WEEK 1: INTRODUCTION & ASSEMBLY

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Students will assemble mBot, identify components, test with IR remote

#### Materials Needed
- mBot kits (1 per student or pair)
- AA batteries (4 per mBot)
- IR remote controls
- Assembly instruction sheets
- Component identification worksheets
- Safety guidelines handout

#### Setup (15 min before class)
- Place one mBot kit at each workspace
- Ensure batteries are available
- Have instruction manuals ready
- Set up example assembled mBot at front

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Introduction (10 min)

**Script:**
> "Welcome to mBot Robotics! Over the next 10 weeks, you'll learn to build and program robots. By the end, you'll create your own robot project to show your parents!"

**Activity: What is a Robot?**
- Write on board: "A robot is a machine that can sense its environment and act on it to achieve goals"
- Ask students to name robots they know
- Show examples:
  - Industrial robots (manufacturing)
  - Service robots (vacuum cleaners)
  - Exploration robots (Mars rovers)
  - Everyday automation (ATMs, automatic doors)

**Key Point:** Robots need:
1. Sensors (INPUT) - to sense environment
2. Brain (PROCESSOR) - to make decisions
3. Actuators (OUTPUT) - to take action

**Introduce the mBot:**
- Show assembled mBot
- Demonstrate it moving with IR remote
- Explain they'll build their own TODAY!

---

#### Part 2: Assembly (40 min)

**Safety Briefing (2 min):**
- Small parts - don't put in mouth
- Screwdrivers - point away from body
- Help each other, ask for help if stuck

**Assembly Process:**

*Step 1: Base Assembly (10 min)*
- Attach motors to chassis
- **Common Issue:** Motors must be tight or they'll come loose
- **Tip:** Use small pliers to tighten hex nuts
- Walk around checking motor tightness

*Step 2: Wheels & Ball Caster (5 min)*
- Attach wheels to motors (press firmly)
- Install ball caster at front
- **Check:** Wheels should spin freely

*Step 3: Battery Pack (5 min)*
- Install battery pack holder
- Insert 4 AA batteries (check polarity!)
- Secure with Velcro or ties

*Step 4: mCore Board (10 min)*
- **CRITICAL:** This is the brain of the robot
- Show ports: M1, M2, Port 1-4
- Attach to top of chassis
- Connect motor cables:
  - LEFT motor → M1
  - RIGHT motor → M2
- **Common Error:** Motors switched - will drive backwards (easy to fix later)

*Step 5: Sensors (8 min)*
- Attach ultrasonic sensor to front
  - Connect cable to Port 3
  - **Looks like robot eyes!**
- Attach line follower to bottom front
  - Connect cable to Port 2
  - **Hangs below chassis**

**Assembly Check (2 min):**
Walk around checking:
- [ ] Motors firmly attached
- [ ] Motor cables connected to M1 and M2
- [ ] Ultrasonic sensor in Port 3
- [ ] Line follower in Port 2
- [ ] Batteries installed correctly
- [ ] Power switch accessible

---

#### Part 3: Testing (10 min)

**First Power-On:**
- "Everyone, turn on your mBot using the power switch"
- Should hear: "Dum, dum, dum" tone
- White LED should light up
- If not: check battery installation

**IR Remote Test:**

*Mode A - Manual Control (3 min)*
- Point remote at mBot
- Press arrow buttons
- mBot should respond to commands
- **If backwards:** Switch motor cables!

*Mode B - Obstacle Avoidance (3 min)*
- Press "B" button on remote
- LED turns GREEN
- Place hand in front of mBot
- Should back up and turn away
- **If not working:** Check ultrasonic sensor in Port 3

*Mode C - Line Following (3 min)*
- Press "C" button on remote
- LED turns BLUE
- Place on black line (use kit's line following map)
- Should follow the line
- **If not working:** Check line follower in Port 2

**Troubleshooting Quick Reference:**
| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| No power | Check batteries, check switch |
| Moves backwards | Switch M1/M2 cables |
| Doesn't respond to remote | Check line of sight, try new battery in remote |
| Mode B doesn't work | Check ultrasonic sensor cable in Port 3 |
| Mode C doesn't work | Check line follower cable in Port 2 |

---

#### Part 4: Inputs & Outputs (10 min)

**Teach Back Activity:**
- Draw two columns on board: INPUTS | OUTPUTS
- Students identify each component

**INPUTS (Sensors):**
- Button (on top of mCore)
- Ultrasonic sensor (measures distance)
- Line follower sensor (detects light/dark)
- IR receiver (receives remote signals)
- Light sensor (on mCore board - top)

**OUTPUTS (Actuators):**
- Motors (make it move!)
- LEDs (2 addressable lights on mCore)
- Buzzer (makes sounds)
- IR transmitter (can send signals to other mBots)

**Discussion:**
- "How is the mBot like a living thing?"
- Eyes (ultrasonic) → see
- Ears (IR receiver) → hear commands
- Legs (motors) → move
- Voice (buzzer) → make sounds

---

#### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**
1. "What does INPUT mean?" (Information going IN to the robot)
2. "What does OUTPUT mean?" (Actions the robot takes)
3. "Name one input on the mBot" (ultrasonic, button, line follower)
4. "Name one output on the mBot" (motors, LEDs, buzzer)

**Preview Next Week:**
- "Next week we'll learn to PROGRAM the mBot using mBlock software"
- "We'll make the LEDs blink in different colors!"
- "Make sure to bring your curiosity and creativity!"

**Storage:**
- Label each mBot with student/pair name
- Turn OFF mBots
- Store safely (designated shelves/bins)
- Collect IR remotes (keep in instructor kit)

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Timing Adjustments:**
- If running long: Skip detailed explanation of Mode B/C, just demonstrate
- If ahead: Let students experiment with different remote commands
- If very ahead: Have students race mBots in manual mode

**Differentiation:**
- **Faster builders:** Help others, test all three modes thoroughly
- **Struggling builders:** Pair with faster peer, instructor helps with tricky parts
- **Fine motor challenges:** Pre-assemble tricky parts (motors to chassis)

**Common Questions & Answers:**

Q: "Can I take my mBot home?"  
A: "Not today, but you'll create programs that we'll save so your mBot 'remembers' what you taught it!"

Q: "Why is mine going backwards when I press forward?"  
A: "Easy fix! We just need to switch two wires. I'll show you."

Q: "Can I program it to do other things?"  
A: "Yes! That's what we'll learn starting next week. You can make it do almost anything!"

Q: "What if I break it?"  
A: "These robots are sturdy and meant to be used. If something comes loose, we can fix it together. Don't worry!"

**Safety Monitoring:**
- Watch for students standing on chairs (when testing movement)
- Ensure mBots stay away from table edges
- Keep small parts away from younger siblings if present

**Take Photos!**
- Students with completed mBots
- Successful tests
- Share on school social media (with permission)

---

### HOMEWORK/EXTENSION (Optional)

**Think About:**
- What would you want your robot to do?
- Draw a picture of your dream robot
- Find 3 examples of robots or automation at home

**For Advanced Students:**
- Research: How does ultrasonic sensing work? (hint: like a bat!)
- Challenge: Can you make the IR remote control TWO mBots at once?

---

### MATERIALS CHECKLIST FOR WEEK 1

**Per Student/Pair:**
- [ ] mBot kit
- [ ] 4x AA batteries
- [ ] IR remote
- [ ] Instruction manual
- [ ] Component identification worksheet

**For Classroom:**
- [ ] Spare batteries
- [ ] Extra hex keys/screwdrivers
- [ ] Small pliers for tightening
- [ ] Line following map
- [ ] Masking tape/labels for mBots
- [ ] Storage bins/shelves

**Handouts:**
- [ ] Safety guidelines
- [ ] Component identification worksheet
- [ ] Parent letter (what we're doing)

---

## WEEK 2: FIRST PROGRAMS - LED CONTROL

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Connect to mBlock, upload first program, control LEDs

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock installed (1 per student/pair)
- USB cables
- mBots (from Week 1)
- Fully charged batteries
- RGB color wheel reference
- Week 2 worksheets

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Software Introduction (15 min)

**Launch mBlock:**
- Guide students to open mBlock
- **Tour of Interface:**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  mBlock                    [Connect] ▼  │
├─────────┬───────────────────┬───────────┤
│         │                   │           │
│  STAGE  │   BLOCK PALETTES  │  SCRIPT   │
│ (Panda) │                   │   AREA    │
│         │   • Motion        │           │
│         │   • Looks         │  (Drag    │
│         │   • Sound         │   blocks  │
│         │   • Pen           │   here)   │
│         │   • Control       │           │
│         │   • Operators     │           │
│         │   • Data & Blocks │           │
│         │   • Robots  ⭐    │           │
│         │                   │           │
└─────────┴───────────────────┴───────────┘
```

**Key Areas:**
1. **Stage:** Where Panda lives (we won't use much for mBot)
2. **Block Palettes:** Where we find programming blocks
3. **Script Area:** Where we build our program
4. **Robots Palette:** 🎯 THIS IS WHERE mBot BLOCKS LIVE!

**Important Concept:**
- "mBlock is based on Scratch - anyone used Scratch before?"
- "Scratch for screen projects, mBlock for robot projects"

---

#### Part 2: Connecting mBot (10 min)

**Connection Process:**

1. **Turn ON mBot** (power switch)
   - Should beep once: "Dum"
   - LED should be white
   - This means "ready for mBlock"

2. **Plug in USB cable**
   - USB-A (big) → Computer
   - USB-B (small/square) → mBot
   - Computer may show "Installing driver" (first time)

3. **In mBlock: Connect Menu**
   - Click "Connect" at top
   - Select "Serial Port"
   - Choose: COM port (Windows) or /dev/tty.wchusbserial (Mac)
   - Should see: "Serial Port Connected" at top

**Troubleshooting:**
- No serial ports shown? 
  - Try different USB port
  - Check cable is fully inserted
  - Restart mBlock
- Multiple ports shown?
  - Try each until "Connected" appears
  - Usually the highest COM number on Windows

**Check Success:**
- Top of mBlock says "Serial Port Connected" ✓
- mBot is on ✓
- Ready to program! ✓

---

#### Part 3: First Program - LED Blink (25 min)

**Introduce the Program Structure:**

```
When mBot Program starts
   ┌──────────────────────┐
   │ Set LED1 to RED      │
   │ Wait 1 second        │
   │ Set LED1 to OFF      │
   │ Wait 1 second        │
   └──────────────────────┘
   Forever
```

**Building the Program (Step-by-Step):**

*Step 1: Start with Hat Block (2 min)*
- Click "Robots" palette (orange)
- Drag "mBot Program" block to script area
- This says "Start here!"

*Step 2: Add Forever Loop (2 min)*
- Click "Control" palette (yellow)
- Drag "forever" block under mBot Program
- Snaps together like Lego!

*Step 3: Set LED to Red (5 min)*
- Back to "Robots" palette
- Find "set led [led on board] [1] red [255] green [0] blue [0]"
- Drag INSIDE forever loop

**Explain RGB Colors:**
- LED makes colors by mixing Red, Green, Blue
- Each color: 0 (off) to 255 (brightest)
- RED: R=255, G=0, B=0
- GREEN: R=0, G=255, B=0
- BLUE: R=0, G=0, B=255
- BLACK (off): R=0, G=0, B=0
- WHITE: R=255, G=255, B=255

*Step 4: Add Wait (3 min)*
- "Control" palette
- "wait [1] secs"
- Drag under LED block

*Step 5: Turn LED Off (3 min)*
- Duplicate the set LED block (right-click → duplicate)
- Change all colors to 0 (black = off)

*Step 6: Add Another Wait (2 min)*
- Another "wait [1] secs" block

**Program Should Look Like:**
```
[mBot Program]
  forever
    set led [led on board] [1] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
    wait [1] secs
    set led [led on board] [1] red [0] green [0] blue [0]
    wait [1] secs
```

---

*Step 7: Upload to mBot! (5 min)*

**IMPORTANT - Two Ways to Run:**

**Method 1: Test in mBlock (Live Mode)**
- Click the mBot Program hat block
- Code runs on computer, sends commands over USB
- Good for testing
- ⚠️ Slower, needs computer connected

**Method 2: Upload to mBot (Standalone)**
- Click "Edit" → "Arduino Mode"
- Code window appears on right
- Click "Upload to Arduino" button
- Wait for upload (15-30 seconds)
- Unplug USB - mBot runs program by itself!
- ✓ This is what we want!

**Upload Process:**
1. Switch to Arduino Mode
2. Click "Upload to Arduino"
3. Wait for "Upload Finished"
4. LED should start blinking RED!
5. Unplug USB, turn off/on mBot
6. Still blinking! It's saved!

**Troubleshooting Upload:**
| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| "mBot not connected" error | Check USB cable, reconnect |
| Upload stuck | Press reset button on mBot, try again |
| "Unsupported block" error | Make sure all blocks are from Robots/Control/Operators palettes only |
| Upload says success but doesn't run | Turn mBot off/on |

---

#### Part 4: Experimentation (10 min)

**Challenge 1: Different Colors (5 min)**
"Change your program so the LED blinks GREEN instead of RED"
- R=0, G=255, B=0
- Upload again!

**Challenge 2: Both LEDs (3 min)**
"Make BOTH LEDs light up - LED1 and LED2"
- Change [1] to [all] in the set led block
- Or add another set led block for LED2

**Challenge 3: Two Colors (2 min)**
"Make LED1 blink red and LED2 blink green at the same time"
- Need TWO set led blocks (one for each LED)

**Example Solution:**
```
[mBot Program]
  forever
    set led [led on board] [1] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
    set led [led on board] [2] red [0] green [255] blue [0]
    wait [1] secs
    set led [led on board] [all] red [0] green [0] blue [0]
    wait [1] secs
```

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Vocabulary Review:**
- **Hat Block:** Starting block (mBot Program)
- **Loop:** Repeat forever
- **Wait:** Pause for time
- **Upload:** Send program to mBot to save it
- **RGB:** Red-Green-Blue color system

**Show and Tell:**
- 2-3 volunteers demonstrate their programs
- "What colors did you choose? Why?"

**Save Your Work:**
- File → Save Project
- Name it: "Week2_YourName_LED"
- Save to designated folder

**Preview Week 3:**
- "Next week: Make the mBot SING!"
- "We'll use the buzzer to play music"

- Yellow light (1 second)
- Green light (3 seconds)
- Repeat

Bring your design next week to code it!

### ANSWER KEY - CHALLENGES

**Challenge 1: GREEN LED**
```
Change: red [0] green [255] blue [0]
```

**Challenge 2: Both LEDs**
```
set led [led on board] [all] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
```

**Challenge 3: Different Colors**
```
set led [led on board] [1] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
set led [led on board] [2] red [0] green [255] blue [0]
wait [1] secs
set led [led on board] [all] red [0] green [0] blue [0]
```

**Extension: Traffic Light**
```
[mBot Program]
  forever
    set led [all] red [255] green [0] blue [0]  // RED
    wait [3] secs
    set led [all] red [255] green [255] blue [0]  // YELLOW
    wait [1] secs
    set led [all] red [0] green [255] blue [0]  // GREEN
    wait [3] secs
```

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Student Struggles:**

1. **"I can't find the block!"**
   - Guide them to correct palette
   - Show color coding
   - Have them describe what they're looking for

2. **"My LED isn't blinking!"**
   - Check uploaded (not just clicked)
   - Check LED number (1, 2, or all)
   - Check colors not all zero
   - Check wait blocks are there

3. **"How do I make purple/orange/etc?"**
   - Show RGB color wheel
   - Purple: R=128, G=0, B=128
   - Orange: R=255, G=165, B=0
   - Let them experiment!

4. **"Upload button isn't working"**
   - Must be in Arduino Mode
   - Must be connected
   - Try Upload to Arduino (not Edit Arduino IDE)

**Timing Adjustments:**
- If running behind: Skip Challenge 3, do as homework
- If ahead: Introduce "play tone" block preview for next week

**Take Photos:**
- Students' colorful LED programs running
- Screens showing their code
- Excited faces!

## WEEK 3-7 DETAILED LESSON PLANS

## TROUBLESHOOTING GUIDE

### Hardware Issues

#### mBot Won't Turn On
**Symptoms:** No sound, no lights when switch turned on
**Solutions:**
1. Check battery polarity (+ and - correct?)
2. Try fresh batteries
3. Check battery connector is plugged into mCore
4. Try different battery pack
5. Last resort: Contact Makeblock support

#### Motors Not Working / Spinning Wrong Direction
**Symptoms:** mBot doesn't move, or moves opposite to commands
**Solutions:**
1. Check motor cables are firmly connected
2. M1 = Left motor, M2 = Right motor
3. If backwards: Swap M1 and M2 cables
4. If weak: Check batteries
5. If one motor doesn't work: Check screw tightness, try swapping motor cables to test if motor or controller issue

#### Ultrasonic Sensor Not Detecting
**Symptoms:** Obstacle avoidance doesn't work, distance always 0 or 400
**Solutions:**
1. Check cable plugged into Port 3
2. Check sensor isn't obstructed
3. Try with flat surface (book) as obstacle
4. Check sensor reading in mBlock (live mode)
5. Distance reads in cm (2-400 range)

#### Line Follower Not Working
**Symptoms:** Line following mode does nothing, or doesn't follow line
**Solutions:**
1. Check cable plugged into Port 2
2. Line must be 2cm wide black tape on white surface
3. Check lighting (no shadows on track)
4. Clean sensor with soft cloth
5. Test sensor values: 0=both on, 1=right off, 2=left off, 3=both off

---

### Software Issues

#### Can't Install mBlock
**Solutions:**
1. Download from official site: www.mblock.cc
2. Windows: Right-click, "Run as Administrator"
3. Mac: Go to Security Settings, allow app
4. Check system requirements
5. Disable antivirus temporarily during install

#### Arduino Driver Won't Install
**Solutions:**
1. mBlock → Connect → Install Arduino Driver
2. Windows: May need to manually install from driver folder
3. Mac: May need signed driver (search Makeblock forums)
4. Try different USB port
5. Restart computer after install

#### Can't Connect to mBot
**Symptoms:** No serial port shown, or connection fails
**Solutions:**
1. Check mBot is ON
2. Check USB cable firmly connected both ends
3. Try different USB cable
4. Try different USB port on computer
5. Restart mBlock
6. Windows: Check Device Manager for COM ports
7. Mac: Check /dev/tty.usbserial appears

#### Upload Fails / Errors During Upload
**Solutions:**
1. Check "Serial Port Connected" shown at top
2. Make sure in Arduino Mode (Edit → Arduino Mode)
3. Check for "Unsupported blocks" dialog
4. Remove any Stage/Sprite blocks (Say, Ask, etc.)
5. Press reset button on mBot, wait 2 seconds, try upload again
6. Close other programs using serial ports
7. Last resort: Connect → Reset Default Program, then upload again

#### Program Uploads But Doesn't Run
**Solutions:**
1. Turn mBot off and on again
2. Check correct blocks used (from Robots palette)
3. Check starts with "mBot Program" hat block
4. Test in Scratch mode first (click hat block)
5. Check batteries charged
6. Upload again

---

### Programming Issues

#### mBot Moves Erratically
**Causes & Solutions:**
- **Low battery:** Replace/charge batteries
- **Speed too high:** Reduce motor speed (try 100-150)
- **Surface too slippery:** Move to rougher surface
- **Motors loose:** Tighten motor screws
- **Code error:** Check motor commands make sense

#### Colors Wrong on LEDs
**Causes & Solutions:**
- **RGB values wrong:** Check R/G/B values (0-255 range)
- **LED number wrong:** Check [1], [2], or [all]
- **Not turning off:** Add "all black" (0,0,0) command
- **Upload issue:** Upload again

#### Ultrasonic Giving Wrong Readings
**Causes & Solutions:**
- **Too close/far:** Works best 5-100cm
- **No settling time:** Add 0.2 second wait before reading
- **Angled surface:** Use flat surface perpendicular to sensor
- **Multiple reads:** Average several readings
- **Interference:** Keep mBots far apart (ultrasonic can interfere)

#### Line Follower Not Accurate
**Causes & Solutions:**
- **Speed too fast:** Slow down (50-80 speed)
- **Line too narrow:** Use 2cm wide black tape
- **Poor contrast:** Ensure black on white
- **Lighting issues:** Avoid shadows, reflective surfaces
- **Sensor dirty:** Clean with soft, dry cloth
- **Algorithm issue:** Review if-then logic

---

## ASSESSMENT RUBRICS

### Weekly Participation Rubric

| Criteria | Not Yet (0) | Developing (1) | Proficient (2) | Exemplary (3) |
|----------|-------------|----------------|----------------|---------------|
| **Attendance & Preparation** | Frequently absent or unprepared | Sometimes absent, usually prepared | Regular attendance, always prepared | Perfect attendance, helps others prepare |
| **Engagement** | Often distracted or off-task | Participates when prompted | Actively engaged most of the time | Highly engaged, enthusiastic learner |
| **Following Instructions** | Needs constant reminders | Follows some instructions | Follows instructions independently | Follows and helps clarify for others |
| **Problem-Solving** | Gives up easily, needs help | Tries briefly before asking | Persists, uses resources | Persistent, creative problem-solver |
| **Collaboration** | Doesn't work well with partner | Works with partner when asked | Collaborates effectively | Exceptional teammate, helps others |
| **Respect for Materials** | Misuses equipment | Careless with equipment | Careful with equipment | Models excellent care |

**Weekly Score: _____ / 18**

---

### Final Project Rubric (Week 10)

| Criteria | Emerging (1) | Developing (2) | Proficient (3) | Advanced (4) | Score |
|----------|--------------|----------------|----------------|---------------|-------|
| **Functionality** | Project doesn't work; meets <50% of requirements | Partially works; meets 50-75% of requirements | Works reliably; meets all basic requirements | Exceeds requirements; polished features | __/4 |
| **Programming Concepts** | Uses 1-2 concepts, minimal structure | Uses 2-3 concepts, some structure | Uses 3+ concepts, well-organized | Excellent structure, advanced techniques, comments | __/4 |
| **Sensor Usage** | No sensors or used incorrectly | 1 sensor used appropriately | 2+ sensors used effectively | Creative sensor integration, handles edge cases | __/4 |
| **Creativity/Originality** | Basic copy of example | Some original elements | Original project or creative twist | Highly innovative, unique approach | __/4 |
| **Code Quality** | Disorganized, hard to understand | Some organization, mostly understandable | Well-organized, custom blocks, readable | Exemplary organization, efficient, well-documented | __/4 |
| **Presentation** | Unclear explanation, incomplete demo | Adequate explanation, demo works | Clear explanation, smooth demo, describes how it works | Excellent presentation, technical depth, engages audience | __/4 |
| **Problem-Solving** | Minimal evidence of iteration | Some testing/fixes evident | Clear evidence of testing and improvement | Sophisticated debugging, multiple iterations, learned from failures | __/4 |
| **Teamwork** | Limited collaboration | Some collaboration, uneven contributions | Balanced contributions, effective teamwork | Exceptional collaboration, leveraged strengths | __/4 |

**Total Score: _____ / 32**

**Grade Conversion:**
- 28-32: Outstanding (A)
- 24-27: Excellent (B)
- 20-23: Good (C)
- 16-19: Satisfactory (D)
- <16: Needs Improvement

<a name="welcome"></a>
## 🤖 Welcome to mBot Robotics!

### What is a Robot?

A **robot** is a machine that can:
1. **SENSE** its environment (using sensors)
2. **THINK** about what to do (using a computer brain)
3. **ACT** on its decisions (using motors and other outputs)

### Your mBot Has:

**INPUTS (Sensors):**
- 👁️ Ultrasonic sensor (like robot eyes - measures distance)
- 🔲 Line follower sensor (detects light and dark)
- 🔘 Button (on top of the robot)
- 📡 IR receiver (receives remote control signals)
- 💡 Light sensor (measures brightness)

**OUTPUTS (Actuators):**
- 🦿 Motors (make it move!)
- 💡 LEDs (colored lights)
- 🔊 Buzzer (makes sounds)
- 📡 IR transmitter (sends signals)

**BRAIN:**
- 🧠 mCore board (like a mini computer)

### My Goals for This Course

Write 3 things you want to learn or create:

1. _____________________________________________

2. _____________________________________________

3. _____________________________________________

---

<a name="week1"></a>
## WEEK 1: Build Your Robot! 🔧

### What I Learned Today:

- ☐ What a robot is
- ☐ How to assemble my mBot
- ☐ What inputs and outputs are
- ☐ How to test with the IR remote

### Assembly Checklist

- ☐ Motors attached tightly to chassis
- ☐ Wheels attached to motors
- ☐ Ball caster installed
- ☐ Battery pack installed with 4 AA batteries
- ☐ mCore board attached
- ☐ Left motor connected to M1
- ☐ Right motor connected to M2
- ☐ Ultrasonic sensor connected to Port 3
- ☐ Line follower sensor connected to Port 2
- ☐ Power switch turns robot ON/OFF
- ☐ IR remote has battery installed

### Testing Results

**Mode A - Manual Control:**
- Forward button works: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Backward button works: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Left turn works: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Right turn works: ☐ Yes ☐ No

**Mode B - Obstacle Avoidance:**
- LED turns green: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Detects my hand: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Backs up and turns: ☐ Yes ☐ No

**Mode C - Line Following:**
- LED turns blue: ☐ Yes ☐ No
- Follows line: ☐ Yes ☐ No

- mCore board
- Motors (M1 and M2)

- Line follower sensor

- Button
- Wheels

│                                     │
│                                     │
│                                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## WEEK 4: Button Control & Decisions 🔘

### What I Learned Today:

- ☐ How to use the button sensor
- ☐ What "if-then" statements do

### If-Then in Real Life

**Give 3 examples of if-then logic from everyday life:**

1. IF _________________, THEN _________________

2. IF _________________, THEN _________________

3. IF _________________, THEN _________________

### Button Program Planning

**Program 1: Simple Button Response**

```
When mBot Program starts
  Wait until [button pressed]
  
  What should happen?
  ______________________________
  ______________________________
```

**Program 2: Different Responses**

```
IF button pressed once:
  Do: ___________________________

IF button pressed again:
  Do: ___________________________
```

### Challenge: Interactive Robot

**Design a program where the mBot responds differently to:**

**First button press:**
- Sound: _______________________
- Light: _______________________
- Movement: ____________________

**Second button press:**
- Sound: _______________________
- Light: _______________________
- Movement: ____________________

### If-Then-Else Practice

**Complete these logic statements for your program:**

```
IF (button is pressed)
  THEN: _______________________
  ELSE: _______________________
```

### Program Flowchart

**Draw a flowchart for your button-controlled program:**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────┐
│                                     │
│         START                       │
│           ↓                         │
│         [   ]                       │
│           ↓                         │
│      < Decision >                   │
│       /        \                    │
│      /          \                   │
│   [YES]        [NO]                 │
│     ↓            ↓                  │
│   [   ]        [   ]                │
│                                     │
│   Draw your flowchart here          │
│                                     │

```

|-------|-------------|--------------|---------|---------------------|
| 0     |             |              |         |                     |
| 1     |             |              |         |                     |
| 2     |             |              |         |                     |
| 3     |             |              |         |                     |

### Line Following Algorithm

**Complete the logic:**

```
Forever:
  
  Read line follower sensor value
  
  IF value = 0 (both on line):
    Action: _______________________
    
  IF value = 1 (right sensor off):
    Action: _______________________
    
  IF value = 2 (left sensor off):
    Action: _______________________
    
  IF value = 3 (both off line):
    Action: _______________________
```

<a name="reference"></a>
## 🔧 Reference Guide

### RGB Color Chart

| Color | Red | Green | Blue |
|-------|-----|-------|------|
| Red | 255 | 0 | 0 |
| Green | 0 | 255 | 0 |
| Blue | 0 | 0 | 255 |
| Yellow | 255 | 255 | 0 |
| Cyan | 0 | 255 | 255 |
| Magenta | 255 | 0 | 255 |
| White | 255 | 255 | 255 |
| Black (OFF) | 0 | 0 | 0 |
| Orange | 255 | 165 | 0 |
| Purple | 128 | 0 | 128 |
| Pink | 255 | 192 | 203 |

### Musical Note Frequencies

| Note | Frequency | Note | Frequency |
|------|-----------|------|-----------|
| C4 | 262 | G4 | 392 |
| D4 | 294 | A4 | 440 |
| E4 | 330 | B4 | 494 |
| F4 | 349 | C5 | 523 |

### Line Follower Sensor Values

| Value | Meaning | Action |
|-------|---------|--------|
| 0 | Both sensors on line | Go straight |
| 1 | Right sensor off line | Turn left |
| 2 | Left sensor off line | Turn right |
| 3 | Both sensors off line | Stop / lost line |

### mBot Port Connections

| Port | Default Device |
|------|----------------|
| M1 | Left Motor |
| M2 | Right Motor |
| Port 1 | (Available) |
| Port 2 | Line Follower |
| Port 3 | Ultrasonic Sensor |
| Port 4 | (Available) |

### Programming Blocks Quick Reference

**Start Program:**
- `[mBot Program]` - Always start with this!

**Loops:**
- `forever` - Repeat forever
- `repeat [10]` - Repeat specific times
- `repeat until < >` - Repeat until condition true

**Decisions:**
- `if < > then` - Do something if condition true
- `if < > then ... else` - Choose between two options

**Wait:**
- `wait [1] secs` - Pause for time
- `wait until < >` - Wait for condition

**Motors:**
- `run [forward] at speed [100]` - Move robot
- `set motor [M1] speed [100]` - Control one motor

**LEDs:**
- `set led [led on board] [1] red [R] green [G] blue [B]`

**Sound:**
- `play tone on note [C4] beat [Quarter]`

**Sensors:**
- `ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance` - Get distance
- `line follower [port 2]` - Get line sensor value
- `button [pressed]` - Check if button pressed

### Troubleshooting Guide

**mBot won't turn on:**
- ☐ Check batteries installed correctly
- ☐ Try fresh batteries
- ☐ Check power switch

**Can't connect to computer:**
- ☐ Check USB cable plugged in both ends
- ☐ Turn mBot ON
- ☐ Try different USB port
- ☐ Restart mBlock

**Program won't upload:**
- ☐ Check "Serial Port Connected" shown
- ☐ Switch to Arduino Mode
- ☐ Remove unsupported blocks
- ☐ Try upload again

**mBot moves backwards:**
- ☐ Switch M1 and M2 motor cables

**Ultrasonic sensor not working:**
- ☐ Check connected to Port 3
- ☐ Add wait 0.2 sec before reading

**Line follower not working:**
- ☐ Check connected to Port 2
- ☐ Use black line on white surface
- ☐ Clean sensor with soft cloth

- BLUE: R=0, G=0, B=255
- YELLOW: R=255, G=255, B=0
- CYAN: R=0, G=255, B=255
- MAGENTA: R=255, G=0, B=255
- WHITE: R=255, G=255, B=255
- BLACK: R=0, G=0, B=0

### Worksheet 3A - Note Frequencies

C4=262, D4=294, E4=330, F4=349, G4=392, A4=440, B4=494, C5=523

### Worksheet 5A - Comparison Operators

1. 15 < 30
2. 50 > 20
3. 25 = 25

### Worksheet 7A - Line Follower Values

- 0: Both on line → Go straight
- 1: Right off line → Turn left
- 2: Left off line → Turn right
- 3: Both off line → Stop/search

- Week-by-week activities

- Certificate of completion
- Can be used on tablets/laptops
- Students can type or draw digitally

### 3. **Printable Worksheets** (1-2 pages per week)
- Ready to print on-site
- Can also be pre-printed
- Includes answer keys
- Activities, planning sheets, reflection forms

**Recommended Printing:**
- **Facilitator Guide:** Print 1 master copy, place in 3-ring binder with dividers

- **Worksheets:** Print weekly as needed OR pre-print full set

## WEEKS 3-7 DETAILED LESSON PLANS

---

## WEEK 3: SOUND & MUSIC - PROGRAMMING THE BUZZER

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Program buzzer to play notes, create variables, build custom blocks, compose melodies

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock installed
- USB cables
- mBots with charged batteries
- Musical note frequency chart
- Week 3 worksheets
- Speakers/headphones (if buzzer too quiet)

#### Setup (15 min before class)
- Ensure all computers connected to network
- Have musical note chart displayed/printed
- Pre-load example melody program
- Test one mBot's buzzer volume
- Have backup batteries ready

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Introduction to Sound & Variables (15 min)

**Review (3 min):**
- "Last week we controlled LEDs - what are LEDs?" (Output device, colored lights)
- "This week we'll control another output - the buzzer!"
- Show buzzer location on mBot (on mCore board)

**Sound Demonstration (5 min):**

*Demo 1: Single Note*
- Load pre-made program that plays C4 (262 Hz)
- Upload and play for class
- "The buzzer plays different frequencies = different notes"

*Demo 2: Scale*
- Play C major scale (C, D, E, F, G, A, B, C)
- "Like a piano keyboard - each note has a number (frequency)"

**Musical Note Frequencies (2 min):**

Display chart:
```
┌──────────────────────────┐
│  MUSICAL NOTE VALUES     │
├──────────────────────────┤
│  C4 = 262 Hz            │
│  D4 = 294 Hz            │
│  E4 = 330 Hz            │
│  F4 = 349 Hz            │
│  G4 = 392 Hz            │
│  A4 = 440 Hz            │
│  B4 = 494 Hz            │
│  C5 = 523 Hz            │
└──────────────────────────┘
```

**Introducing Variables (5 min):**

Write on board:
```
play tone on note [262] beat [Quarter]
```

**Problem:** "If I want to play C4 many times, I have to remember 262 is C4. What if I forget?"

**Solution: VARIABLES!**

"A variable is like a labeled box that holds a value."

```
┌─────────┐
│   C4    │  ← Label (variable name)
│  = 262  │  ← Value it holds
└─────────┘
```

**Why use variables?**
1. **Readable:** See "C4" instead of "262"
2. **Reusable:** Change value in ONE place
3. **Organized:** Code easier to understand

**Real-world analogy:**
- Your name is a "variable" that holds your identity
- Your phone number is a "variable" that holds a number
- Much easier to remember "Mom's phone" than the actual number!

---

#### Part 2: Creating Variables & Playing Notes (20 min)

**Creating Your First Variable (5 min):**

**Step-by-step with class:**

1. Click "Data & Blocks" palette (orange)
2. Click "Make a Variable" button
3. Type variable name: `Note_C4`
   - **Important:** Start with letter (not number)
   - Use underscore _ for spaces
   - NO SPACES allowed in variable names
4. Select "For all sprites" (global)
5. Click OK

**You'll see:**
- Checkbox with "Note_C4" appears
- Variable is created but has NO VALUE yet

**Setting Variable Value (3 min):**

1. Find "set [Note_C4] to [0]" block in Data & Blocks palette
2. Drag under "mBot Program" hat block
3. Change [0] to [262]

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
```

**Now variable Note_C4 holds the value 262!**

**Using the Variable (4 min):**

1. Go to "Robots" palette
2. Find "play tone on note [C4] beat [Quarter]"
3. Drag under the set block
4. **Instead of typing 262:** Drag the Note_C4 variable from Data & Blocks palette into the note slot

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
  play tone on note [Note_C4] beat [Quarter]
```

**Upload and Test!**
- Click "Edit" → "Arduino Mode"
- Click "Upload to Arduino"
- Should hear one note!

**Create All Note Variables (8 min):**

"Now let's create variables for a whole scale!"

**Students create 8 variables:**
- Note_C4 = 262
- Note_D4 = 294
- Note_E4 = 330
- Note_F4 = 349
- Note_G4 = 392
- Note_A4 = 440
- Note_B4 = 494
- Note_C5 = 523

**Facilitator circulates helping students**

**Quick tip:** Have students work in pairs - one creates variables, other sets values, then switch

---

#### Part 3: Custom Blocks & Melodies (20 min)

**The Problem with Repetition (3 min):**

Show this code:
```
[mBot Program]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
  set [Note_D4] to [294]
  ...
  play tone on note [Note_C4] beat [Quarter]
  play tone on note [Note_D4] beat [Quarter]
  play tone on note [Note_E4] beat [Quarter]
  play tone on note [Note_F4] beat [Quarter]
  ...
```

**Ask:** "What's repeated here?"
- Answer: "play tone on note [___] beat [Quarter]"

**Teach:** "When code repeats, we can use a CUSTOM BLOCK!"

**Custom blocks are like creating your own LEGO brick**
- You design it once
- Use it many times
- Makes code cleaner and easier to read

---

**Creating Custom "Play" Block (7 min):**

**Step-by-step:**

1. Click "Data & Blocks" palette
2. Click "Make a Block" button
3. Type: `Play`
4. Click arrow next to "Options"
5. Click "Add number input"
6. Click on "number1" and change to `Note`
7. Click OK

**You'll see two things:**
- A new hat block: `define Play [Note]`
- A new block in palette: `Play [Note]`

**Now build the Play block:**

Under the "define Play [Note]" hat:
1. Drag "play tone on note [C4] beat [Quarter]" block
2. Drag the purple `Note` from the hat block into the note slot

```
define Play [Note]
  play tone on note [Note] beat [Quarter]
```

**This custom block now plays ANY note we give it!**

---

**Using Custom Blocks (5 min):**

Now in your main program:
```
[mBot Program]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
  set [Note_D4] to [294]
  set [Note_E4] to [330]
  set [Note_F4] to [349]
  set [Note_G4] to [392]
  set [Note_A4] to [440]
  set [Note_B4] to [494]
  set [Note_C5] to [523]
  
  Play [Note_C4]
  Play [Note_D4]
  Play [Note_E4]
  Play [Note_F4]
  Play [Note_G4]
  Play [Note_A4]
  Play [Note_B4]
  Play [Note_C5]
```

**Upload and test!**
- Should play full C major scale
- Much cleaner code!

**DRY Principle (2 min):**

Write on board: **D.R.Y. = Don't Repeat Yourself**

"Professional programmers follow DRY principle"
- If you're copying/pasting code → make a custom block instead
- Easier to fix bugs (only one place to change)
- Easier to read and understand

---

**Challenge: Compose a Melody (3 min):**

"Now create your own melody!"

**Simple melodies to try:**
- Mary Had a Little Lamb: E D C D E E E
- Hot Cross Buns: E D C, E D C
- Twinkle Twinkle: C C G G A A G

**Extension:** Add a variable for "Rest" (silence)
```
set [Rest] to [0]
Play [Rest]  ← Creates a pause
```

---

#### Part 4: Adding Visual Effects (Optional - 5 min)

**LED Light Show with Music:**

"Let's make our robot more fun - add lights!"

**Example:**
```
[mBot Program]
  ... (initialize variables)
  
  Play [Note_C4]
  set led [all] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
  
  Play [Note_D4]
  set led [all] red [0] green [255] blue [0]
  
  Play [Note_E4]
  set led [all] red [0] green [0] blue [255]
```

**Challenge:** Make LEDs change color with each note!

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**

1. **"What is a variable?"**
   - Answer: A named container that holds a value

2. **"Why use variables?"**
   - Easier to read, change value in one place, organized code

3. **"What is a custom block?"**
   - A block you create that can be reused

4. **"What is the DRY principle?"**
   - Don't Repeat Yourself - use custom blocks for repeated code

**Share Time (2 min):**
- 2-3 volunteers play their melodies
- Class guesses the song (if it's a known tune)

**Preview Next Week:**
- "Next week: BUTTONS!"
- "Make your robot interactive - respond to button presses"
- "We'll make a button-controlled music player"

**Save Work:**
- File → Save Project
- Name: "Week3_YourName_Music"

**Turn Off mBots:**
- Power switch to OFF
- Disconnect USB cables
- Store safely

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Issues & Solutions:**

1. **"Can't hear the buzzer!"**
   - Buzzer is quiet - this is normal
   - Use in quieter environment
   - Have students lean close to mBot
   - Consider connecting speakers if available

2. **"Variable name error!"**
   - Must start with letter (not number)
   - No spaces (use underscore)
   - No special characters except underscore

3. **"Upload fails - unsupported block!"**
   - Make sure using "play tone on note" (not "play note")
   - Check all variables are initialized before use

4. **"Note sounds wrong!"**
   - Check frequency value
   - Make sure variable set BEFORE it's used
   - Verify correct variable is being used

5. **"Custom block not working!"**
   - Check variable is passed to play tone block
   - Make sure "define Play" block exists
   - Verify note duration is set

**Timing Adjustments:**

- **If running behind:** Skip LED light show, assign as homework
- **If ahead:** Introduce repeat loops for repeated notes
- **For advanced students:** Introduce note duration variable

**Differentiation:**

**For struggling students:**
- Provide pre-made variable setup
- Give them specific melody to code (with note sequence)
- Pair with stronger peer

**For advanced students:**
- Create multiple custom blocks (PlayLong, PlayShort)
- Add note duration as parameter
- Compose longer melody (16+ notes)
- Create musical game (press button to play note)

**Extension Ideas:**

1. **Musical Simon Says:**
   - Robot plays sequence
   - Student must press button to repeat it

2. **Note Duration:**
   - Add second parameter to Play block for duration
   - `define Play [Note] [Duration]`

3. **Multiple Melodies:**
   - Create custom blocks: PlayVerse, PlayChorus
   - Build song structure

**Take Photos/Videos:**
- Students creating variables
- Successful melody playback
- Enthusiastic reactions
- Share on school social media

---

### HOMEWORK/EXTENSION (Optional)

**Design a Musical Alarm:**
- Plays wake-up tune when button pressed
- Uses at least 8 notes
- Includes LED light show
- Due: Next week (optional showcase)

**Research:**
- How does sound work? (vibrations)
- What is frequency? (vibrations per second)
- Why do different notes sound different?
