## WEEK 4: BUTTON CONTROL & CONDITIONAL LOGIC

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Use button sensor, program if-then logic, create interactive programs

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- USB cables  
- mBots with charged batteries
- Week 4 worksheets
- Flowchart template handouts

#### Setup (15 min before class)
- Pre-load example button program
- Have if-then logic flowchart displayed
- Prepare button demo mBot
- Review previous week's melody programs

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Introduction to Conditionals (15 min)

**Review & Connect (3 min):**

"Last week we made music automatically - press upload and it plays."

**Ask:** "What if we want control over WHEN it plays?"

**Today's Answer:** BUTTONS! Make robot interactive.

---

**Real-World If-Then Logic (5 min):**

**Activity: "Everyday Conditionals"**

"We use if-then logic every day!"

**Ask students to complete:**
- "IF it's raining, THEN I ___________" (bring umbrella)
- "IF I'm hungry, THEN I ___________" (eat food)
- "IF alarm rings, THEN I ___________" (wake up)
- "IF button pressed, THEN robot ___________" (??)

**Write on board:**
```
IF (condition is true)
  THEN (do this action)
```

**Key Point:** Computers make decisions using if-then logic!

---

**The Button on mBot (3 min):**

**Show on mBot:**
- Button location (on top of mCore board)
- Press it - hear click
- It's a momentary switch (only on while pressed)

**Button States:**
- **Pressed:** Button is pushed down
- **Released:** Button is not pushed

"Today we'll program mBot to do different things when button pressed!"

---

**Demo: Button-Triggered Sound (4 min):**

**Show pre-loaded program:**
```
[mBot Program]
  wait until [button pressed]
  play tone on note [Note_C4] beat [Whole]
```

**Upload and demonstrate:**
1. Upload program
2. Press button → hear tone!
3. Press again → hear tone again!

**Ask:** "What's happening?"
- Program WAITS until button pressed
- When pressed → plays note
- Program ends

**Problem:** "Only plays once! Let's fix that..."

---

#### Part 2: Wait Until vs. Forever + If-Then (20 min)

**Two Ways to Check Button (5 min):**

**Method 1: Wait Until (one-time action)**
```
[mBot Program]
  wait until [button pressed]
  (do something once)
```

**Method 2: Forever + If-Then (continuous checking)**
```
[mBot Program]
  forever
    if [button pressed] then
      (do something every time)
```

**Analogy:**
- Wait Until = "Stand at door until pizza arrives, then eat"
- Forever + If = "Keep checking door. If pizza there, eat a slice"

---

**Building Wait Until Program (5 min):**

**Students code along:**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Note_E4] to [330]
  set [Note_D4] to [294]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
  
  wait until [button pressed]
  
  Play [Note_E4]
  Play [Note_D4]
  Play [Note_C4]
  Play [Note_D4]
  Play [Note_E4]
  Play [Note_E4]
  Play [Note_E4]
```

*(Mary Had a Little Lamb)*

**Finding Button Block:**
1. Go to "Robots" palette
2. Find "button [pressed]" block
3. It's HEXAGONAL (decision shape!)
4. Fits in "wait until" block

**Upload and Test:**
- Program waits
- Press button → plays melody!
- **Problem:** Only plays once, then program ends

---

**Building Forever + If-Then Program (10 min):**

**Introduce If-Then Block:**

"Let's make it play EVERY time we press button!"

**Need:**
- Forever loop (keep checking)
- If-then block (make decision)

**Step-by-step:**

1. **Start with hat block**
   ```
   [mBot Program]
   ```

2. **Add forever loop**
   ```
   [mBot Program]
     forever
   ```

3. **Add if-then inside forever**
   ```
   [mBot Program]
     forever
       if <  > then
   ```

4. **Add button block to if**
   - Drag "button [pressed]" into hexagon
   ```
   [mBot Program]
     forever
       if [button pressed] then
   ```

5. **Add action inside if-then**
   ```
   [mBot Program]
     forever
       if [button pressed] then
         Play [Note_C4]
         wait [0.5] secs
   ```

**Important:** Add small wait! Why?
- Button check happens VERY fast
- Without wait: plays note many times per press
- With wait: plays once per press

**Upload and Test:**
- Press button → plays note
- Press again → plays note again!
- Works forever!

---

#### Part 3: If-Then-Else (Two Choices) (15 min)

**The Problem (2 min):**

"What if we want DIFFERENT actions for different button presses?"

**Example:**
- First press → Play happy sound
- Second press → Play sad sound

**Solution:** If-Then-Else!

---

**Introducing If-Then-Else (5 min):**

**Draw on board:**
```
       (Check condition)
             ↓
         <Decision>
         /        \
      YES          NO
       ↓            ↓
   (Action A)   (Action B)
```

**In mBlock:**
- Use "if <  > then... else" block (from Control palette)
- Has TWO sections: top for YES, bottom for NO

**Example scenario:**
```
IF (button pressed):
  THEN: Turn LED green
ELSE:
  Turn LED red
```

---

**Building Toggle Program (8 min):**

"Let's build a program that changes behavior!"

**Concept:** Use a variable to track state

**Code structure:**
```
[mBot Program]
  set [Mode] to [1]
  
  forever
    if [button pressed] then
      
      if [Mode] = [1] then
        (Do action 1)
        set [Mode] to [2]
        
      else
        (Do action 2)
        set [Mode] to [1]
      
      wait [1] secs  (prevent multiple presses)
```

**Complete Example:**
```
[mBot Program]
  set [Mode] to [1]
  set [Note_C4] to [262]
  set [Note_G4] to [392]
  
  forever
    if [button pressed] then
      
      if [Mode] = [1] then
        Play [Note_C4]
        set led [all] red [0] green [255] blue [0]
        set [Mode] to [2]
      else
        Play [Note_G4]
        set led [all] red [255] green [0] blue [0]
        set [Mode] to [1]
      
      wait [1] secs
```

**How it works:**
1. Mode starts at 1
2. Press button: Mode=1? Yes → Play C4, change to Mode 2
3. Press again: Mode=1? No → Play G4, change back to Mode 1
4. Alternates forever!

---

#### Part 4: Challenge Activities (10 min)

**Challenge 1: Musical Instrument (5 min)**

"Make a simple piano!"

**Requirements:**
- Button plays different note each press
- At least 4 different notes
- Cycles through notes

**Hint:** Use variable to track which note to play

---

**Challenge 2: Interactive Light Show (3 min)**

"Button controls LED show!"

**Requirements:**
- Each button press changes LED color
- At least 5 different colors
- Make pattern interesting

---

**Challenge 3: Pattern Game (2 min)**

"Can you remember the pattern?"

**Requirements:**
- Robot plays sequence (e.g., high-low-high)
- Press button 3 times to repeat
- LEDs show if correct

*(Advanced - may need hints from facilitator)*

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**

1. **"What does IF-THEN do?"**
   - Makes decisions - IF condition true, THEN do action

2. **"Difference between Wait Until and Forever+If?"**
   - Wait Until = one time, Forever+If = continuous checking

3. **"What is If-Then-Else?"**
   - Chooses between TWO actions based on condition

4. **"Why add small wait after button check?"**
   - Prevents multiple rapid triggers

**Vocabulary Review:**
- **Conditional:** Statement that makes decision
- **Boolean:** True or False value
- **Toggle:** Switch between two states
- **State:** Current condition or mode

**Preview Next Week:**
- "Next week: ULTRASONIC SENSOR!"
- "Make robot SEE objects"
- "Stop before hitting obstacles"

**Save & Store:**
- Save: "Week4_YourName_Button"
- Turn off mBots
- Store safely

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Issues:**

1. **"Button doesn't respond!"**
   - Check button is on mCore board (not remote)
   - Make sure uploaded to mBot (not just running in mBlock)
   - Press firmly but not too hard

2. **"Plays too many times per press!"**
   - Add wait block after button check
   - Need 0.5-1 second wait

3. **"Toggle doesn't work!"**
   - Check Mode variable initialized
   - Make sure Mode changes in both if and else
   - Verify comparison uses = not other operator

4. **"Program ends after one press!"**
   - Need forever loop!
   - If-then must be INSIDE forever

**Differentiation:**

**For struggling students:**
- Provide partially completed program
- Focus on simple wait until program first
- Pair with peer mentor

**For advanced students:**
- Challenge 3 (pattern game)
- Use button release (not just pressed)
- Create button counter (how many presses?)
- Long press vs. short press detection

**Extension Ideas:**

1. **Button Debouncing:**
   - Teach proper button handling
   - Detect press vs. hold

2. **Multi-Button Patterns:**
   - If additional buttons available
   - Create combinations

3. **Timing Game:**
   - Press button at right time
   - LEDs show timing window

---

### HOMEWORK/EXTENSION

**Design Interactive Robot:**
- Choose: Music player OR Light show OR Game
- Must use button input
- Must have at least 3 different states/modes
- Draw flowchart of logic

**Bring next week to share!**

---

### MATERIALS CHECKLIST FOR WEEK 4

**Per Student/Pair:**
- ☐ Computer with mBlock
- ☐ USB cable
- ☐ mBot with charged batteries
- ☐ Week 4 worksheets
- ☐ Flowchart template

**For Classroom:**
- ☐ If-then logic poster
- ☐ Example button programs
- ☐ Extra batteries
- ☐ Flowchart symbols reference

## WEEK 5: ULTRASONIC SENSOR - DISTANCE DETECTION

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Understand ultrasonic sensor operation, read distance values, program obstacle detection

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- USB cables
- mBots with charged batteries
- Measuring tape/rulers (cm)
- Various objects for distance testing (books, boxes)
- Week 5 worksheets

#### Setup (15 min before class)
- Have measuring tapes at each station
- Pre-load distance reading demo program
- Prepare obstacle course area
- Test ultrasonic sensor range

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Introduction to Sensors & Ultrasonic (15 min)

**Hook: Animal Senses (3 min)**

**Ask:** "How do animals sense their environment?"

**List on board:**
- Dogs: smell, hearing
- Eagles: vision
- Bats: echolocation
- Sharks: electric fields
- Cats: whiskers

**Connect:** "Robots need sensors to 'sense' like animals!"

---

**How Bats "See" (4 min)**

**Explain echolocation:**

"Bats are blind, so how do they fly in dark caves?"

**ECHOLOCATION:**
1. Bat makes high-pitched sound (ultrasonic)
2. Sound bounces off objects
3. Bat hears echo
4. Brain calculates distance from time delay

**Draw on board:**
```
  Bat → ))))) → | Wall
  Bat ← ((((( ← | Wall
  
  Fast echo = close
  Slow echo = far
```

**Ultrasonic = Sound too high for humans to hear**
- Bats: 20,000-120,000 Hz
- Humans hear: 20-20,000 Hz
- Dogs hear higher than humans!

---

**Ultrasonic Sensor on mBot (5 min)**

**Show sensor:**
- Two "eyes" on front of mBot
- Left eye: TRANSMITTER (sends sound)
- Right eye: RECEIVER (hears echo)

**Demonstration:**

1. Turn on mBot
2. Wave hand in front of sensor
3. "Invisible sound waves bouncing!"

**How it works:**
```
Sensor → ))) → Hand
Sensor ← ((( ← Hand
mBot calculates: Time × Speed = Distance
```

**Technical details (optional for advanced):**
- Speed of sound ≈ 343 meters/second
- Sensor measures time in microseconds
- Converts to centimeters automatically!

---

**Sensor Range & Limitations (3 min)**

**Write on board:**
```
┌────────────────────────────┐
│ ULTRASONIC SENSOR          │
├────────────────────────────┤
│ Minimum distance: 2 cm     │
│ Maximum distance: 400 cm   │
│ Best range: 5-100 cm       │
│ Returns: distance in cm    │
└────────────────────────────┘
```

**Limitations:**
- Doesn't work well on soft/angled surfaces (absorbs sound)
- Works best on flat, hard surfaces
- Affected by very loud noises
- Small objects might not be detected

**Good obstacles:** Books, walls, hands, boxes
**Bad obstacles:** Pillows, curtains, angled surfaces

---

#### Part 2: Reading Distance Values (20 min)

**Demo: Reading Sensor (5 min)**

**Show program:**
```
[mBot Program]
  forever
    say [ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance] for [1] secs
    wait [0.2] secs
```

**Note:** This only works in Scratch Mode (running from mBlock)

**Upload and demonstrate:**
1. Run program (click hat block)
2. Move hand toward sensor
3. Numbers change!
4. Measure with ruler - accurate?

---

**Student Activity: Distance Experiments (10 min)**

**Students work in pairs:**

**Task:** Measure and record actual vs. sensor distance

**Worksheet activity:**
| Object | Predicted (cm) | Sensor Reading | Actual (cm) | Difference |
|--------|---------------|----------------|-------------|------------|
| Hand   |               |                |             |            |
| Book   |               |                |             |            |
| Wall   |               |                |             |            |

**Process:**
1. Predict distance
2. Read sensor
3. Measure with ruler
4. Calculate difference

**Discussion questions:**
- Are readings accurate?
- What affects accuracy?
- Which objects work best?

---

**Understanding the Block (5 min)**

**Show in mBlock:**

```
[ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance]
```

**Key points:**
- Found in "Robots" palette (orange)
- OVAL shape = reports a number
- **port 3** = where sensor plugged in
- Returns distance in centimeters
- Updates continuously

**Port Check:**
- Ultrasonic MUST be in Port 3
- If in wrong port, won't work!
- Check cable connection

---

#### Part 3: Comparison Operators & LED Indicator (15 min)

**Introducing Comparison Operators (5 min)**

"Now we'll use distance to make decisions!"

**Show operators (from Operators palette):**
```
<  > = Less than
<  > = Greater than  
<  > = Equal to
```

**Practice:**
- 10 < 20 → TRUE
- 30 > 15 → TRUE
- 25 = 25 → TRUE
- 50 < 20 → FALSE

**Ask:** "If distance < 15, what does that mean?"
- Answer: Object is CLOSE (less than 15 cm away)

---

**LED Distance Indicator Program (10 min)**

"Let's make a distance indicator using LEDs!"

**Plan:**
- GREEN = Safe (>30 cm)
- YELLOW = Caution (15-30 cm)
- RED = Danger (<15 cm)

**Build together:**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Distance] to [0]
  
  forever
    set [Distance] to [ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance]
    wait [0.2] secs  ← Important! Sensor settling time
    
    if [Distance] > [30] then
      set led [all] red [0] green [255] blue [0]  ← GREEN
    
    if [Distance] < [30] and [Distance] > [15] then
      set led [all] red [255] green [255] blue [0]  ← YELLOW
    
    if [Distance] < [15] then
      set led [all] red [255] green [0] blue [0]  ← RED
```

**Important concepts:**

1. **Store distance in variable** - Read sensor once per loop
2. **Wait 0.2 seconds** - Sensor needs time for accurate reading
3. **Use if-then** (not if-then-else) - All conditions checked
4. **Compound conditions** - Using AND operator for range

**Upload and test:**
- Move hand toward sensor
- Watch LED colors change!
- Check distances with ruler

---

#### Part 4: Stop Before Obstacle (10 min)

**The Challenge:**

"Make mBot move forward and STOP before hitting obstacle!"

**Requirements:**
- Move forward
- Stop when obstacle <15 cm
- Don't hit the obstacle!

---

**Solution - Guided Build (8 min):**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Distance] to [

**human**: Continue

**assistant**:  ```
[mBot Program]
  set [Distance] to [0]
  
  forever
    set [Distance] to [ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance]
    wait [0.1] secs
    
    if [Distance] > [15] then
      run [forward] at speed [80]
    else
      run [forward] at speed [0]
```

**Explanation:**

"Let's think through the logic:"

1. **Check distance** continuously
2. **IF** distance > 15 cm (obstacle far away)
   - **THEN** move forward at speed 80
3. **ELSE** (obstacle close - 15 cm or less)
   - Stop motors (speed = 0)

**Key Points:**

- **Speed 80** (not 150+) - Slower = more control
- **Distance > 15** - Gives stopping distance
- **Wait 0.1 secs** - Fast enough response
- **Forever loop** - Continuous checking

---

**Testing & Refinement (2 min):**

**Test procedure:**
1. Place mBot on floor
2. Put book/box 30 cm away
3. Upload program
4. Observe: Does it stop before hitting?

**If it hits obstacle:**
- Increase distance threshold (try 20 cm)
- Decrease speed (try 60)
- Check sensor is clean

**Challenge students:**
"Can you get it to stop EXACTLY 10 cm from obstacle?"
- Need to experiment with threshold
- Each mBot may be slightly different

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**

1. **"How does ultrasonic sensor work?"**
   - Sends sound, measures echo time, calculates distance

2. **"What do comparison operators do?"**
   - Compare numbers: <, >, =

3. **"Why read sensor into variable first?"**
   - Only read once per loop, use same value in all decisions

4. **"Why add wait after reading sensor?"**
   - Sensor needs time to get accurate reading

5. **"Why use slow speed for obstacle detection?"**
   - Gives time to stop, more accurate

**Real-World Applications:**

Ask: "Where else is ultrasonic sensing used?"

- Parking sensors in cars
- Automatic doors
- Liquid level detection
- Blind assistance devices
- Drone obstacle avoidance

**Preview Next Week:**
- "Continuous obstacle avoidance"
- "Make mBot navigate autonomously"
- "Robot moves by itself, avoiding everything!"

**Save & Store:**
- Save: "Week5_YourName_Ultrasonic"
- Clean sensor with soft cloth if dirty
- Store carefully

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Issues & Solutions:**

1. **"Sensor gives weird readings!"**
   - Check cable in Port 3
   - Clean sensor with soft cloth
   - Check batteries charged
   - Try different obstacle (hard, flat surface)
   - Add longer wait (0.2-0.3 secs)

2. **"mBot hits obstacle anyway!"**
   - Speed too fast → reduce to 50-80
   - Threshold too small → increase to 20 cm
   - Battery low → replace/charge
   - Surface too slippery → use rougher surface

3. **"Distance always shows 400 or 0!"**
   - 400 = nothing detected (out of range)
   - 0 = error or too close (<2 cm)
   - Check sensor connection
   - Check port setting in block

4. **"LED doesn't change colors correctly!"**
   - Check if-then conditions (not overlapping?)
   - Verify distance variable being updated
   - Check RGB values correct

**Timing Adjustments:**

- **If running behind:** Skip LED indicator, focus on stop program
- **If ahead:** Add challenge: stop at different distances with different LED colors

**Differentiation:**

**For struggling students:**
- Provide pre-built LED indicator program
- Focus on understanding comparison operators
- Give specific distance values to test

**For advanced students:**
- Create "parking assistant" (beep faster as closer)
- Multiple distance zones with different sounds
- Graph distance over time (if using Stage)
- Calculate speed of object approaching

**Safety Notes:**
- Keep mBots on floor or large tables
- Clear area of obstacles that could damage mBot
- Watch for mBots driving off table edges
- Test area before letting all students run programs

**Extension Ideas:**

1. **Theremin:**
   - Distance controls tone frequency
   - Closer = higher pitch
   - Music with no touching!

2. **Distance Alarm:**
   - Beeps when someone gets too close
   - Faster beeps = closer person

3. **Automatic Night Light:**
   - Use light sensor AND ultrasonic
   - Turns on LED when dark AND motion detected

---

### HOMEWORK/EXTENSION

**Design Challenge:**

Create a "personal space protector"
- Detects when someone gets too close
- Makes sound AND lights up
- Different reactions for different distances

**Bring diagram/flowchart next week!**

**Research:**
- How do self-driving cars use sensors?
- What other types of distance sensors exist?
- How does sonar in submarines work?

---

### MATERIALS CHECKLIST FOR WEEK 5

**Per Student/Pair:**
- ☐ Computer with mBlock
- ☐ USB cable
- ☐ mBot with charged batteries
- ☐ Measuring tape or ruler (cm)
- ☐ Objects for testing (book, box)
- ☐ Week 5 worksheets

**For Classroom:**
- ☐ Extra batteries (sensor drains faster)
- ☐ Variety of test objects
- ☐ Large space for testing
- ☐ Soft barriers (books, foam) for obstacles
- ☐ Comparison operator reference chart

## WEEK 6: AUTONOMOUS OBSTACLE AVOIDANCE

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Program continuous obstacle avoidance, create navigation strategy, understand autonomous behavior

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- USB cables
- mBots with FULLY charged batteries
- Obstacle course materials (boxes, books, cones, chairs)
- Large open space (2m × 3m minimum)
- Week 6 worksheets

#### Setup (15 min before class)
- Create simple obstacle course
- Have complex course ready for later
- Ensure large clear testing area
- Pre-load example autonomous program
- Charge ALL batteries (this lesson drains them fast!)

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: What is Autonomous? (10 min)

**Hook: Self-Driving Cars (3 min)**

"Who has heard of self-driving cars?"

**Show image or video (if possible):**
- Tesla, Waymo, other autonomous vehicles
- No driver needed!

**Ask:** "How does the car know where to go?"
- Sensors (cameras, ultrasonic, lidar, radar)
- Computer brain makes decisions
- No human controlling it!

---

**Defining Autonomous (4 min)**

**Write on board:**

```
AUTONOMOUS = Can make decisions 
              and act on its own
              WITHOUT human control
```

**Examples:**

| AUTONOMOUS | NOT AUTONOMOUS |
|------------|----------------|
| Roomba vacuum | Remote control car |
| Self-driving car | Drone with pilot |
| Mars rover | Video game character |
| Factory robot | Toy with button |

**Key difference:** Does it make its OWN decisions?

---

**Last Week vs. This Week (3 min)**

**Last week:**
- mBot moved forward
- Stopped at obstacle
- **Then what?** NOTHING! Just stopped.

**This week:**
- mBot moves forward
- Detects obstacle
- **Avoids it**
- Continues moving
- **Does this FOREVER - no human needed!**

**This is AUTONOMOUS behavior!**

---

#### Part 2: Designing Avoidance Strategy (15 min)

**The Problem (3 min)**

"When mBot hits obstacle, what should it do?"

**Brainstorm with class:**
- Stop (we did this!)
- Back up (good idea!)
- Turn (which way?)
- Go forward again (yes!)

**Write strategy on board:**
```
1. Move forward
2. IF obstacle detected:
   a. Stop
   b. Back up
   c. Turn (left or right?)
   d. Continue forward
3. Repeat forever
```

---

**Decision: Turn Left or Right? (5 min)**

**Discuss:**

"Should mBot always turn the same direction?"

**Strategy 1: Always turn right**
- Pros: Simple, predictable
- Cons: Might get stuck in corners

**Strategy 2: Always turn left**
- Pros: Simple, predictable  
- Cons: Might get stuck in corners

**Strategy 3: Random turn**
- Pros: Less likely to get stuck
- Cons: More complex code
- Needs random number

**For today:** Let's use "always turn right" (simple!)

**Advanced:** Can add random later

---

**Creating Custom Blocks (7 min)**

"Let's organize our code with custom blocks!"

**Three custom blocks we'll create:**

**1. detectObstacle**
```
define detectObstacle
  set [Distance] to [ultrasonic sensor [port 3] distance]
  wait [0.2] secs
  if [Distance] < [15] then
    set [ObstacleDetected] to [1]
  else
    set [ObstacleDetected] to [0]
```

**What it does:** Checks if obstacle close, sets flag

---

**2. avoidObstacle**
```
define avoidObstacle
  run [forward] at speed [0]  ← Stop
  wait [0.5] secs
  
  run [backward] at speed [80]  ← Back up
  wait [1] secs
  
  run [forward] at speed [0]  ← Stop
  wait [0.3] secs
  
  run [turn right] at speed [100]  ← Turn
  wait [0.6] secs
  
  run [forward] at speed [0]  ← Stop
```

**What it does:** Complete avoidance sequence

---

**3. moveForward**
```
define moveForward
  run [forward] at speed [80]
```

**What it does:** Simple forward movement

**Why custom blocks?**
- Organized code
- Easy to modify
- Easy to debug
- Reusable

---

#### Part 3: Building the Program (20 min)

**Initialize Variables (3 min)**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Distance] to [0]
  set [ObstacleDetected] to [0]
  set [Speed] to [80]
```

**Variables:**
- **Distance:** Current sensor reading
- **ObstacleDetected:** Flag (1=yes, 0=no)
- **Speed:** Forward movement speed

---

**Main Program Logic (7 min)**

**Build together step-by-step:**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [Distance] to [0]
  set [ObstacleDetected] to [0]
  set [Speed] to [80]
  
  wait until [button pressed]  ← Safety! Don't start immediately
  wait [2] secs  ← Get hand away!
  
  forever
    moveForward
    detectObstacle
    
    if [ObstacleDetected] = [1] then
      avoidObstacle
```

**Walk through logic:**

1. **Start:** Initialize variables
2. **Wait:** For button press (safety!)
3. **Loop forever:**
   - Move forward at speed
   - Check for obstacles
   - IF obstacle found:
     - Execute avoidance
     - Continue loop

---

**Build Custom Blocks (10 min)**

**Students create all 3 custom blocks:**

**Facilitator walks around helping**

**Common issues to watch for:**
- Forgetting to initialize variables
- Wrong port for ultrasonic sensor
- Turn timing too short/long
- Speed too fast

**Testing each block:**
1. Test detectObstacle first (add LED indicator)
2. Test avoidObstacle (manually trigger)
3. Test complete program

---

#### Part 4: Obstacle Course Challenge (15 min)

**Simple Course (5 min)**

**Start with basic obstacle course:**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────┐
│  START                          │
│    ↓                            │
│  [📦] ← Obstacle 1             │
│                                 │
│        [📦] ← Obstacle 2       │
│                                 │
│  [📦] ← Obstacle 3             │
│    ↓                            │
│  FINISH (or continues forever!) │
└─────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Students test their programs:**
- Upload program
- Press button to start
- Observe behavior
- Make adjustments

**Questions to ask:**
- Does it avoid all obstacles?
- Does it get stuck anywhere?
- Is speed good?
- Does turn timing work?

---

**Complex Course (5 min)**

**Increase difficulty:**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────┐
│  START                          │
│    ↓                            │
│  [📦][📦] ← Multiple obstacles │
│                                 │
│    [📦]                        │
│ [📦]   [📦] ← Scattered        │
│         [📦]                   │
│                                 │
│  [📦][📦][📦] ← Narrow passage│
└─────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Challenge:**
"Can your mBot navigate this course?"

**Adjustments needed:**
- May need to tune turn timing
- May need to adjust speed
- May need different detection distance

---

**Class Discussion (5 min)**

**Gather class together:**

**Ask:**
1. "What worked well?"
2. "What was challenging?"
3. "Why do different mBots behave differently?"
4. "What could make avoidance better?"

**Answers to expect:**
- Battery charge affects speed/turns
- Motor variations affect movement
- Surface friction affects turns
- Sensor reading variations
- Random obstacles hard to predict

**Key insight:** "Good enough" is often better than "perfect"
- Real robots deal with uncertainty
- Must adapt and iterate
- Testing is crucial!

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**

1. **"What does autonomous mean?"**
   - Makes own decisions without human control

2. **"What are the steps in our avoidance strategy?"**
   - Detect, stop, back up, turn, continue

3. **"Why use custom blocks?"**
   - Organization, readability, reusability

4. **"Why did some mBots behave differently?"**
   - Battery levels, motor variations, surface differences

**Real-World Connection:**

"Where else is autonomous navigation used?"
- Warehouse robots (Amazon)
- Delivery robots
- Autonomous vehicles
- Drones
- Mars rovers
- Robotic lawn mowers

**Preview Next Week:**
- "LINE FOLLOWING!"
- "mBot follows a path"
- "New sensor: Line follower"
- "Different kind of navigation"

**Important Note:**
- Turn OFF mBots (save battery!)
- This lesson drains batteries fast
- Charge before next week

**Save:**
- "Week6_YourName_Autonomous"

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Issues & Solutions:**

1. **"mBot drives in circles!"**
   - Turn timing wrong
   - One motor weaker than other
   - Adjust turn wait time
   - Try 0.4-0.8 seconds range

2. **"mBot hits obstacles anyway!"**
   - Speed too fast → reduce to 60-70
   - Detection distance too small → increase to 20 cm
   - Sensor not updating → check wait time
   - Battery low → replace/charge

3. **"mBot backs into things!"**
   - Back up time too long → reduce
   - OR: Add rear obstacle detection (advanced)

4. **"Gets stuck in corners!"**
   - Always-turn-same-direction limitation
   - Try different turn angle
   - Consider random turn (extension)

5. **"Batteries die quickly!"**
   - Motors drain batteries fast
   - Have multiple sets charged
   - Limit run time per session
   - Consider LiPo batteries (rechargeable)

**Timing Adjustments:**

- **If running behind:** 
  - Skip complex obstacle course
  - Provide pre-built custom blocks
  - Focus on main program only

- **If ahead:**
  - Add random turn direction
  - Create competitive obstacle course
  - Time how long to navigate course

**Differentiation:**

**For struggling students:**
- Provide completed custom blocks
- Focus on main program structure
- Simplify obstacle course
- Pair with advanced peer

**For advanced students:**
- Add random turn direction:
  ```
  set [RandomTurn] to [pick random [1] to [2]]
  if [RandomTurn] = [1] then
    (turn left)
  else
    (turn right)
  ```
- Add sound effects for obstacles
- Try to avoid same obstacle twice
- Track number of obstacles avoided

**Safety:**

- Keep testing area clear
- Watch for mBots near table edges
- Don't let mBots run unattended
- Turn off when not testing
- Catch mBots before they hit walls hard

**Extension Ideas:**

1. **Multiple Strategies:**
   - Try different avoidance patterns
   - Compare effectiveness

2. **Optimization:**
   - Minimize time to navigate course
   - Minimize battery usage

3. **Multi-Bot:**
   - Can multiple mBots avoid each other?
   - (Hint: yes! ultrasonic detects other mBots)

---

### HOMEWORK/EXTENSION

**Design Challenge:**

**"The Ultimate Obstacle Avoider"**

Design improvements to avoidance strategy:
- Draw flowchart
- Explain why it's better
- What makes it more efficient?

**Research:**
- How do warehouse robots navigate?
- What sensors do self-driving cars use?
- How does Mars Curiosity rover explore?

## WEEK 7: LINE FOLLOWING

### LESSON PLAN

**Duration:** 60 minutes  
**Objectives:** Understand line follower sensor, implement line following algorithm, program path navigation

#### Materials Needed
- Computers with mBlock
- USB cables
- mBots with charged batteries
- Black electrical tape (2cm wide)
- White poster board or smooth floor space
- Line following track (from mBot kit or custom-made)
- Week 7 worksheets
- Stopwatch for lap timing

#### Setup (20 min before class)
- Create line following tracks with black tape
- Test tracks with one mBot
- Ensure good lighting (no shadows on track)
- Have multiple tracks for different difficulty levels
- Clean all line follower sensors

---

### LESSON BREAKDOWN

#### Part 1: Introduction to Line Following (12 min)

**Real-World Examples (3 min)**

"Where have you seen robots following paths?"

**Examples:**
- Factory automated guided vehicles (AGVs)
- Warehouse robots
- Airport baggage systems
- Delivery robots on sidewalks
- Robotic lawn mowers (boundary wire)

**Why line following?**
- Predictable paths
- No GPS needed indoors
- Simple and reliable
- Good for factories/warehouses

---

**How Does Line Follower Sensor Work? (5 min)**

**Show sensor on mBot:**
- Located on bottom front of chassis
- Two pairs of infrared (IR) sensors
- Each pair: one emitter, one receiver

**Explain infrared:**
- IR = Invisible light
- Like TV remote
- Can detect light and dark surfaces

**How it works:**
```
Sensor pair diagram:

[LED]     [LED]        ← IR emitters (send light)
  ↓         ↓
 )))       )))         ← IR light
  ↓         ↓
─────────────────     ← Surface (black or white)
  ↑         ↑
 (((       (((         ← Reflected light
  ↑         ↑
[Receiver][Receiver]   ← IR receivers (detect light)

WHITE surface: Reflects lots of IR → Sensor "sees" light
BLACK surface: Absorbs IR → Sensor "sees" dark
```

**Key Point:**
- Black absorbs light (sensor detects less reflection)
- White reflects light (sensor detects more reflection)
- Sensor can tell difference!

---

**Understanding Sensor Values (4 min)**

**The line follower returns 4 possible values:**

**Write on board:**
```
┌──────────────────────────────────────┐
│  LINE FOLLOWER SENSOR VALUES         │
├──────────────────────────────────────┤
│  Value 0: Both sensors ON line      │
│           ═══║═══  (both black)      │
│           Action: GO STRAIGHT        │
│                                      │
│  Value 1: Right sensor OFF line     │
│           ═══╬     (right white)     │
│           Action: TURN LEFT          │
│                                      │
│  Value 2: Left sensor OFF line      │
│               ╬═══  (left white)     │
│           Action: TURN RIGHT         │
│                                      │
│  Value 3: Both sensors OFF line     │
│                     (both white)     │
│           Action: STOP/SEARCH        │
└──────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Visual demonstration:**
- Show mBot line follower sensor
- Place on track
- Move across line
- Show values in mBlock (Scratch mode if possible)

---

#### Part 2: Building Line Follower Program (23 min)

**Testing Sensor Values (5 min)**

**Quick test program (Scratch mode only):**
```
[When mBot Program starts]
  forever
    say [line follower [port 2]] for [0.5] secs
```

**Students test on track:**
- Both sensors on line → see "0"
- Right sensor off → see "1"
- Left sensor off → see "2"
- Both off → see "3"

**Important:** Line must be ~2cm wide, black on white

---

**Algorithm Design (5 min)**

**Write algorithm on board together:**

```
Forever:
  Read line follower sensor
  
  IF value = 0 (both on line):
    GO STRAIGHT
    
  IF value = 1 (right off line):
    TURN LEFT (gently)
    
  IF value = 2 (left off line):
    TURN RIGHT (gently)
    
  IF value = 3 (both off line):
    STOP (lost the line!)
```

**Key insight:** "Gentle" corrections!
- Not big turns, just slight adjustments
- Think: steering a car, not spinning

---

**Building the Program (13 min)**

**Step 1: Initialize (2 min)**
```
[mBot Program]
  set [LineSensor] to [0]
  set [Speed] to [80]
  set [TurnSpeed] to [60]
```

---

**Step 2: Main Loop Structure (3 min)**
```
[mBot Program]
  set [LineSensor] to [0]
  set [Speed] to [80]
  set [TurnSpeed] to [60]
  
  wait until [button pressed]
  wait [1] secs
  
  forever
    set [LineSensor] to [line follower [port 2]]
    wait [0.05] secs  ← Quick response needed!
    
    (conditions go here)
```

**Why short wait (0.05 secs)?**
- Line following needs FAST response
- Robot moving quickly
- Must detect changes immediately

---

**Step 3: Add Conditions (8 min)**

**Build all four conditions:**

```
[mBot Program]
  set [LineSensor] to [0]
  set [Speed] to [80]
  set [TurnSpeed] to [60]
  
  wait until [button pressed]
  wait [1] secs
  
  forever
    set [LineSensor] to [line follower [port 2]]
    wait [0.05] secs
    
    if [LineSensor] = [0] then
      run [forward] at speed [Speed]
    
    if [LineSensor] = [1] then
      set motor [M1] speed [TurnSpeed]  ← Left motor slower
      set motor [M2] speed [Speed]       ← Right motor normal
    
    if [LineSensor] = [2] then
      set motor [M1] speed [Speed]       ← Left motor normal
      set motor [M2] speed [TurnSpeed]  ← Right motor slower
    
    if [LineSensor] = [3] then
      run [forward] at speed [0]  ← Stop if lost line
```

**Explain steering technique:**

"Like steering a car:"
- Want to turn left? Slow down left wheel
- Want to turn right? Slow down right wheel
- This makes smooth turns!

**Alternative:** Can use tank turns (harder to control)

---

#### Part 3: Testing & Tuning (20 min)

**Start with Simple Track (5 min)**

**Straight line test:**
```
START ═══════════════════════ END
```

**Students upload and test:**
- Does it follow straight line?
- Does it wobble too much?
- Does it stay centered?

**If wobbles:**
- Speed too fast → reduce to 60-70
- Turn too aggressive → adjust TurnSpeed

---

**Gentle Curve Test (5 min)**

**Add curves:**
```
START ═══╗
         ║
         ╚══════ END
```

**Observe:**
- Can it handle curves?
- Does it go off track?
- Too slow or too fast?

**Adjustments:**
- Increase speed if too slow
- Decrease if going off track
- Tune TurnSpeed for smooth steering

---

**Sharp Corner Test (5 min)**

**90-degree corners:**
```
START ═══╗
         ║
         ╚═══ END
```

**This is challenging!**
- May need slower speed
- May need more aggressive turn
- Some wobbling is normal

**Class discussion:**
"Why are sharp corners harder?"
- Answer: Robot momentum, turn radius, sensor position

---

**Complete Circuit (5 min)**

**Full track with straights, curves, and corners:**

**Challenge:** "Complete a full lap without going off track!"

**Time trials (optional):**
- Fastest complete lap wins
- But must stay on track!
- Record times on board

---

### Wrap-Up (5 min)

**Review Questions:**

1. **"How does line follower sensor work?"**
   - IR light, detects reflection from black/white surfaces

2. **"What do the 4 sensor values mean?"**
   - 0=both on, 1=right off, 2=left off, 3=both off

3. **"Why use different motor speeds for turning?"**
   - Creates smooth steering, like a car

4. **"What's the tradeoff between speed and accuracy?"**
   - Fast = less control, Slow = more accurate

5. **"Why might different tracks give different results?"**
   - Line width, surface material, lighting, tape quality

**Real-World Applications:**

"Where is line following used?"
- Warehouse AGVs follow lines
- Factory assembly robots
- Airport baggage systems
- Museum tour robots
- Hospital delivery robots

**Preview Next Week:**
- "Final project planning!"
- "Time to create your OWN robot project"
- "Teams, ideas, design"
- "Two weeks to build something amazing"

**Save:**
- "Week7_YourName_LineFollower"

---

### FACILITATOR NOTES

**Common Issues & Solutions:**

1. **"Can't detect line!"**
   - Check sensor in Port 2
   - Clean sensor with soft, dry cloth
   - Check line is 2cm wide
   - Ensure black on white (good contrast)
   - Check lighting (no shadows or reflections)

2. **"Goes off track immediately!"**
   - Speed too fast → reduce to 50-60
   - TurnSpeed might be same as Speed → make it lower
   - Line too narrow → use wider tape
   - Sensor dirty → clean it

3. **"Wobbles too much (zigzag)!"**
   - Turn corrections too aggressive
   - Increase TurnSpeed (less difference between wheels)
   - Slightly reduce main Speed
   - Check track surface is smooth

4. **"Loses line at corners!"**
   - Speed too fast → slow down (60-70)
   - Sharp corners need slower speed
   - OR: Use both motor control for sharper turns
   - Line might be too narrow

5. **"Works on one track but not another!"**
   - Different tape/surface affects sensor
   - Different lighting
   - Track width differences
   - May need to tune for each track

**Track Building Tips:**

1. **Line specs:**
   - Width: 1.5-2.5cm (2cm ideal)
   - Material: Black electrical tape
   - Surface: White poster board or smooth floor
   - Avoid: Glossy surfaces (reflect too much)

2. **Track design:**
   - Start with straight lines
   - Add gentle curves
   - Then 90-degree corners
   - Finally: S-curves and sharp turns

3. **Testing:**
   - Test track with one mBot first
   - Ensure no tape bubbles or wrinkles
   - Check lighting (no shadows)
   - Mark start/finish clearly

**Differentiation:**

**For struggling students:**
- Simpler track (mostly straight)
- Pre-set Speed values
- Partner with advanced student
- Focus on understanding sensor values

**For advanced students:**
- Complex track with hairpin turns
- Speed optimization challenge
- Create intersection handling
- Add obstacle detection during line following

**Extension Ideas:**

1. **Intersection Detection:**
   - When value = 0 for longer time → intersection
   - Make decision (turn or go straight)

2. **Line Following + Obstacle Avoidance:**
   - Follow line
   - If obstacle detected, avoid it
   - Return to line

3. **Two-Line Following:**
   - Follow right edge of line
   - Or follow left edge
   - More challenging!

---

**Draw:**

## END OF WEEKS 3-7 DETAILED

**assistant**:  ## FACILITATOR MASTER GUIDE - CONTINUED

---

## CONSOLIDATED TROUBLESHOOTING GUIDE (All Weeks)

### HARDWARE TROUBLESHOOTING

#### Power & Battery Issues

| Symptom | Possible Causes | Solutions |
|---------|----------------|-----------|
| mBot won't turn on | • Dead batteries<br>• Battery polarity wrong<br>• Loose battery connector | • Replace all 4 AA batteries<br>• Check + and - alignment<br>• Push connector firmly into mCore |
| Powers on then dies quickly | • Weak batteries<br>• Loose connection | • Use fresh batteries<br>• Recharge LiPo if using<br>• Check all connections tight |
| Inconsistent behavior | • Low battery voltage | • Always replace ALL batteries at once<br>• Don't mix old and new batteries |
| LiPo won't charge | • Bad cable<br>• Not plugged in correctly | • Check USB cable connection<br>• Ensure mBot power switch ON while charging<br>• LED should indicate charging |

**Battery Best Practices:**
- Use quality alkaline or rechargeable AA batteries
- Replace all 4 at same time
- LiPo batteries provide more consistent power
- Keep spare sets charged for class
- Typical runtime: 1-2 hours depending on usage

---

#### Motor Issues

| Symptom | Possible Causes | Solutions |
|---------|----------------|-----------|
| One motor doesn't work | • Cable unplugged<br>• Wrong port<br>• Motor damaged | • Check cable firmly in M1 or M2<br>• Try swapping motors to test<br>• Contact Makeblock if damaged |
| Both motors don't work | • Cables unplugged<br>• Power issue | • Check both motor cables<br>• Check battery power<br>• Try reset/reupload program |
| Moves backwards when should go forward | • Motor cables swapped | • Switch M1 and M2 cables<br>• This is most common build error! |
| Weak/slow movement | • Low batteries<br>• Motors loose<br>• Wheels slipping | • Replace batteries<br>• Tighten motor mounting screws<br>• Check wheels pressed firmly on axles |
| Makes grinding noise | • Loose mounting screws<br>• Damaged gears | • Tighten all motor screws<br>• Check for stripped gears<br>• May need replacement |
| Motors get very hot | • Stalled/blocked<br>• Running at high speed too long | • Check nothing blocking movement<br>• Reduce speed<br>• Add breaks in program |

**Motor Maintenance:**
- Check screws weekly (vibration loosens them)
- Keep small pliers handy for tightening
- Spare motors recommended for large classes
- Motor direction can be swapped in code if needed

---

#### Sensor Issues

**Ultrasonic Sensor (Port 3)**

| Symptom | Solutions |
|---------|-----------|
| Always reads 0 | • Check cable in Port 3<br>• Clean sensor lenses<br>• Check for damage<br>• Too close (<2cm) |
| Always reads 400 | • Nothing detected (normal!)<br>• Check sensor facing forward<br>• Try flatter obstacle |
| Erratic readings | • Add 0.2 sec wait after reading<br>• Check for interference from other mBots<br>• Ensure stable obstacle surface<br>• Check lighting (very bright light can interfere) |
| Doesn't detect obstacles | • Port setting wrong in code<br>• Cable loose<br>• Sensor angled wrong<br>• Obstacle too small/soft |

**Line Follower Sensor (Port 2)**

| Symptom | Solutions |
|---------|-----------|
| Doesn't detect line | • Check cable in Port 2<br>• Clean sensor with soft cloth<br>• Ensure black line on white surface<br>• Check lighting (no shadows) |
| Wrong values | • Port setting wrong in code<br>• Line too narrow (need 2cm)<br>• Glossy surface (too reflective)<br>• Sensor too high/low from surface |
| Works on one track, not another | • Different tape/surface materials<br>• Lighting differences<br>• May need speed adjustment |
| Can't follow curves | • Speed too fast<br>• Turn corrections too aggressive<br>• Tune TurnSpeed variable |

**Button (on mCore)**

| Symptom | Solutions |
|---------|-----------|
| Doesn't respond | • Upload to mBot (doesn't work in Scratch mode)<br>• Add wait time after press<br>• Press firmly but not too hard |
| Triggers multiple times | • Add 0.5-1 sec wait after detection<br>• Debounce in code |

**General Sensor Tips:**
- Always check port numbers match in code
- Clean sensors weekly with soft, dry cloth
- Add wait time after reading for stable values
- Test sensors individually before combining

---

#### Structural Issues

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Wheels fall off | Press firmly onto motor shafts, should hear click |
| Ball caster stuck | Remove and clean, check for debris |
| Chassis cracked | Use clear tape as temporary fix, contact Makeblock for replacement |
| Screws missing | Use spares from kit, or standard M4 screws |
| Loose connections | Use cable ties or tape to secure |

---

### SOFTWARE TROUBLESHOOTING

#### Installation Issues

**mBlock Won't Install**

**Windows:**
```
1. Right-click installer
2. Select "Run as Administrator"
3. Disable antivirus temporarily
4. Check system requirements (Windows 7+)
5. Download latest version from mblock.cc
```

**Mac:**
```
1. Go to System Preferences → Security & Privacy
2. Click "Open Anyway" for mBlock
3. If unsigned driver warning: allow in Security settings
4. May need signed driver from Makeblock forums
```

**Chromebook:**
- Use mBlock web version (requires Chrome browser)
- Bluetooth mBot version only
- Some features limited

---

**Arduino Driver Won't Install**

**Windows:**
```
1. mBlock → Connect → Install Arduino Driver
2. If fails: Manually install from:
   C:\Program Files\mBlock\Arduino\drivers
3. Device Manager → Ports → Update driver
4. Point to driver folder above
5. Restart computer
```

**Mac:**
```
1. May need third-party signed driver
2. Search Makeblock forums for "Mac driver"
3. Create symbolic link if driver name too long:
   - Terminal: cd /dev
   - ln -s cu.wchusbserial1410 cu.usbserial
4. Restart mBlock
```

**Linux:**
- Not officially supported
- Use Wine to run Windows version
- Or use Arduino IDE directly with Makeblock libraries

---

#### Connection Issues

**Can't Connect to mBot**

**Checklist:**
- [ ] mBot turned ON (power switch)
- [ ] USB cable firmly connected both ends
- [ ] Arduino driver installed
- [ ] Correct serial port selected
- [ ] No other programs using serial port
- [ ] Tried different USB port on computer
- [ ] Tried different USB cable
- [ ] Restarted mBlock
- [ ] Restarted computer

**Windows Port Selection:**
```
1. Connect → Serial Port → COM[number]
2. Usually highest COM number
3. If multiple: unplug mBot, see which disappears
4. Check Device Manager → Ports (COM & LPT)
```

**Mac Port Selection:**
```
1. Connect → Serial Port → /dev/tty.wchusbserial[xxx]
2. If multiple devices: unplug to identify
3. Should appear when mBot connected
```

**Still Can't Connect:**
```
1. Try "Reset Default Program" from Connect menu
2. Close all other serial programs
3. Try different computer to isolate issue
4. Check USB cable with other device
5. Contact Makeblock support if hardware issue
```

---

#### Upload Issues

**Program Won't Upload**

| Error Message | Solution |
|--------------|----------|
| "mBot not connected" | Follow connection troubleshooting above |
| "Upload timeout" | • Press reset button on mBot<br>• Wait 2 seconds<br>• Try upload again<br>• Check battery power |
| "Unsupported blocks" | • Remove Stage/Sprite blocks (say, ask, pen, etc.)<br>• Use only Robots, Control, Operators, Data blocks<br>• Check dialog for specific blocks to remove |
| "Compilation error" | • Check code for errors<br>• Variables defined before use?<br>• Correct port numbers?<br>• Valid variable names? |
| Upload success but doesn't run | • Turn mBot off and on<br>• Check starts with "mBot Program" hat<br>• Verify code logic is correct |

**Arduino Mode Upload Process:**
```
1. Edit → Arduino Mode
2. Code appears on right
3. Click "Upload to Arduino"
4. Wait for "Upload Finished" (15-30 seconds)
5. Watch for error messages in grey area below code
```

**Reset to Factory Settings:**
```
If mBot behaving strangely:
1. Connect → Reset Default Program
2. Wait for completion
3. Test with IR remote
4. Upload your program again
```

---

#### Programming Issues

**Variables**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| "Variable not found" | • Create variable first (Data & Blocks → Make a Variable)<br>• Check spelling matches exactly<br>• Check visibility (For all sprites) |
| Variable shows checkbox | Normal - uncheck to hide from Stage |
| Can't use variable | • Drag variable into input (don't type name)<br>• Make sure initialized before use |
| Variable won't change | • Check using "set" block (not "change")<br>• Verify logic flow reaches set block |

**Custom Blocks**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Custom block doesn't work | • Check "define [block]" hat exists<br>• Verify code under define hat<br>• Ensure block is being called in program |
| Parameters not working | • Drag parameter from hat into blocks<br>• Don't type parameter name<br>• Check parameter type matches use |
| Block not in palette | • Refresh mBlock<br>• Create block again if needed |

**Loops & Conditionals**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Forever loop doesn't stop | That's normal! Turn off mBot or upload new program |
| If-then not triggering | • Check condition evaluates to true<br>• Test condition with say block (Scratch mode)<br>• Verify sensor values correct |
| Repeat loop runs wrong times | • Check number is what you intended<br>• Variables can change during loop |

---

### CLASSROOM MANAGEMENT TROUBLESHOOTING

#### Common Classroom Issues

**Time Management**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Running out of time | • Have pre-built example ready<br>• Skip optional extensions<br>• Provide partially completed programs<br>• Focus on core concepts only |
| Students finish too early | • Have extension challenges ready<br>• Advanced worksheets<br>• Help others<br>• Explore additional features |
| Uneven pace | • Pair fast/slow students<br>• Differentiated activities<br>• Self-paced challenges |

**Behavior Management**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Too much excitement/noise | • Establish signal (lights off, robot beep)<br>• Set clear expectations<br>• Reward good behavior |
| Racing/rough play | • Clear rules about mBot handling<br>• Keep mBots on floor only<br>• Designated testing areas<br>• One driver at a time in pairs |
| Not following instructions | • Check understanding with questions<br>• Break into smaller steps<br>• Visual guides<br>• Peer mentoring |
| Off-task behavior | • Engaging challenges<br>• Clear goals<br>• Time limits for activities<br>• Positive reinforcement |

**Technical Management**

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Not enough mBots | • Rotate pairs/groups<br>• While one codes, other documents<br>• Share testing time |
| Computer issues | • Have backup computers<br>• Test all before class<br>• Student chromebooks/tablets<br>• Pair students |
| Network problems | • mBlock works offline<br>• Pre-download updates<br>• Have USB installer ready |
| Storage issues | • Network drive for saving<br>• USB drives for each pair<br>• Cloud storage (Google Drive, etc.)<br>• Email projects to students |

---

### SAFETY GUIDELINES

**Physical Safety**

**mBot Operation:**
- ✓ Keep mBots on floor or low, stable tables
- ✓ Clear area of tripping hazards
- ✓ Watch for mBots near table edges
- ✓ Turn off when not in use
- ✗ Never stand on chairs to watch mBot
- ✗ Don't let mBots drive into walls at high speed
- ✗ Keep away from liquids
- ✗ Don't operate near stairs/drop-offs

**Battery Safety:**
- ✓ Insert batteries with correct polarity
- ✓ Remove batteries if storing long-term
- ✓ Charge LiPo with provided cable only
- ✓ Adult supervision for battery changes
- ✗ Don't mix old and new batteries
- ✗ Don't leave LiPo charging unattended
- ✗ Don't use damaged batteries

**Tool Safety:**
- ✓ Screwdrivers point away from body
- ✓ Adult help with small screws
- ✓ Keep small parts away from young children
- ✗ Don't force screws (strip threads)

**Sensor Safety:**
- ✓ Handle ultrasonic sensor gently
- ✓ Clean with soft, dry cloth only
- ✗ Don't touch sensor lenses with fingers
- ✗ Don't use liquids to clean sensors

---

### Mid-Course Assessment (After Week 4-5)

**Student Name:** _______________ **Date:** _______

**Practical Assessment: "Make a Distance Alarm"**

**Requirements:**
1. Use ultrasonic sensor to detect distance
2. LED turns red when object <20cm
3. LED turns green when object >20cm
4. Plays tone when object very close (<10cm)
5. Runs continuously

**Rubric:**

| Criteria | 0 | 1 | 2 | 3 | Score |
|----------|---|---|---|---|-------|
| **Program Structure** | No hat block or organization | Basic structure, many errors | Good structure, minor errors | Excellent structure, no errors | __/3 |
| **Sensor Use** | Sensor not working | Reads sensor with errors | Reads sensor correctly | Reads sensor, handles edge cases | __/3 |
| **Conditional Logic** | No conditionals or wrong | Some conditions work | All conditions work | Complex conditions, well-organized | __/3 |
| **Outputs** | LEDs/sound don't work | One output works | Both outputs work | Both outputs + additional features | __/3 |
| **Testing** | No evidence of testing | Minimal testing | Good testing, some issues remain | Thorough testing, handles all cases | __/3 |
| **Code Quality** | Disorganized, no comments | Some organization | Well-organized, some comments | Excellent organization, good comments | __/3 |

**Total: _____ / 18**

### Final Project Rubric (Week 10) - DETAILED

**Project Name:** _______________ **Team:** _______

#### 1. FUNCTIONALITY (8 points)

**Does the project work as intended?**

| Level | Description | Points |
|-------|-------------|--------|
| **Not Functional** | Project doesn't work or crashes<br>Meets <25% of stated requirements<br>Major errors prevent demonstration | 0-2 |
| **Partially Functional** | Works inconsistently<br>Meets 25-50% of requirements<br>Some features work, others don't<br>Requires multiple restarts | 3-4 |
| **Mostly Functional** | Works reliably most of the time<br>Meets 50-75% of requirements<br>All major features work<br>Minor bugs don't prevent use | 5-6 |
| **Fully Functional** | Works consistently and reliably<br>Meets all stated requirements (75-100%)<br>Polished, professional result<br>Exceeds basic requirements | 7-8 |

**Score:** _____ / 8

_______________________________________________
